# TOSS Platform Functional Specification v1.0

## Introduction

**TOSS (The One-Stop Solution)** is a next-generation ERP-III platform tailored for South African township and rural businesses. It combines a full suite of ERP modules with intelligent _Service-as-Software (SaaS 2.0)_ features and a _Collaborative Network_ layer to help small businesses not just manage operations, but also gain insights and work together as a community[\[1\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L52-L60)[\[2\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L118-L126). The system is **offline-first and mobile-first**, delivered as a Nuxt 4 Progressive Web App for low-end Android devices, and powered by a multi-tenant, event-driven .NET 8 backend (Clean Architecture with PostgreSQL)[\[3\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L263-L271)[\[4\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L243-L250). Every design choice aligns with ERPNext's proven ERP module concepts[\[5\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L158-L166), adapted to be simpler and more context-appropriate for users like spaza shop owners, hawkers, small-scale manufacturers, and other township entrepreneurs.

**Product Pillars:** The platform consists of three integrated layers[\[6\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L90-L98):

- **ERP-III Modules (Business Backbone):** Traditional ERP domains (Sales, Purchasing, Accounting, Stock, etc.) providing the essential tools to run a business.
- **SaaS 2.0 (AI Business Coach):** An AI-driven layer that watches business data and proactively suggests actions or automations (a "business manager with an MBA" guiding the owner)[\[7\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L110-L118).
- **Collaborative Network:** Multi-tenant capabilities that let independent businesses cooperate - pooling orders, sharing resources, and collectively negotiating as a network[\[8\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L120-L124).

In the sections below, each ERP module is specified in detail - including its purpose, key workflows, business rules, data model, UI/UX expectations (with offline functionality), and an example use case in a township/rural context. Subsequent sections describe how the AI SaaS layer and Collaborative Network layer augment these modules with insights and cross-organization workflows. All functionality is aligned with ERPNext's documented features for familiarity and robustness[\[9\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L160-L169)[\[10\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L176-L183), while ensuring the solution remains **simple, offline-capable, and intuitive** for the target users[\[11\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L54-L61).

## Selling (Sales & Marketing Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Selling module streamlines the entire sales process from first customer contact to final sale, while also helping manage customer relationships. It covers customer inquiries, quotations, sales orders, deliveries, and invoicing, integrating closely with CRM and Accounting. In essence, this module helps businesses **generate and track sales** and maintain customer info to improve service and revenue[\[12\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=The%20Selling%20module%20in%20ERPNext,and%20enhance%20customer%20relationship%20management)[\[13\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/CRM#:~:text=The%20CRM%20module%20in%20ERPNext,interactions%20and%20streamline%20sales%20processes). It also supports basic marketing functions like tracking campaigns or referrals relevant to township businesses (e.g. word-of-mouth promotions).

**Core Workflows:** Key workflows in Selling include:

- **Lead-to-Quote:** Capture a lead or inquiry (via CRM), then create a **Quotation** (sales quote) for the products/services the customer is interested in. Quotations can be emailed or WhatsApped to customers and later converted to orders[\[14\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,on%20sales%20performance%2C%20revenue%2C%20and).
- **Order Fulfillment:** Convert an accepted quotation into a **Sales Order**. The Sales Order is the confirmed customer order, which initiates reservation of stock. From the Sales Order, generate a **Delivery Note** (packing/delivery slip) to ship goods, and finally create a **Sales Invoice** to bill the customer[\[14\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,on%20sales%20performance%2C%20revenue%2C%20and).
- **Direct Sale (POS):** For walk-in or counter sales, use the POS interface (integrated with this module) to quickly create an invoice and record payment on the spot (see **POS module** below for details). POS sales automatically deduct stock and create accounting entries.
- **Returns & Credit Notes:** If a customer returns an item, record a **Sales Return** (Credit Note) which updates stock and creates a credit in the customer's account.
- **Payment Collection:** Track payments against sales invoices (handled in Accounting module but visible in customer account status). Manage accounts receivable and follow up on overdue payments if any.
- **Customer Management:** Maintain a master list of **Customers** with contact info, billing/shipping addresses, and credit terms. This links to CRM for communication history and to Accounting for credit limits and outstanding balances[\[15\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,trends%20to%20inform%20strategic%20decisions).

**Business Rules & Validation:** Several business rules ensure data integrity and proper sales cycles:

- **Quotation Validity:** Quotations have an expiration date; the system prevents converting an expired quote to an order without extension.
- **Stock Reservation:** Confirmation of a Sales Order will reserve stock (or trigger a backorder if stock is insufficient). The system will not allow delivery notes to be submitted for quantities beyond what's in stock or reserved (unless configured to allow negative stock in special cases).
- **Pricing Rules:** The module should support promotional pricing or volume discounts (e.g. buy-one-get-one or bulk price breaks) via a pricing rule engine. When an item is added to a sales order or invoice, applicable price rules are applied automatically[\[16\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=What%20features%20are%20available%20in,the%20Sales%20module).
- **Status Transitions:** Documents follow defined status flows - e.g. Sales Order statuses: Draft → Submitted/Confirmed → Completed (when fully delivered and invoiced) or Cancelled. Delivery Notes cannot be submitted if there is no linked order (configurable) or if required stock is not available. Invoices require an associated Sales Order/Delivery or can be standalone for direct sales.
- **Credit Control:** If a customer has exceeded their credit limit or has overdue invoices, the system can warn or block new sales orders to that customer (based on configuration). This protects businesses from extending too much informal credit.
- **Taxes and Discounts:** Sales transactions calculate taxes (VAT, etc.) as defined. The system validates that required tax fields are filled and calculations are correct. Similarly, if any line or global discounts are given, they must respect configured limits (e.g. an owner might set a max 10% discount for sales staff).

**Data Model & Key Fields:** Important DocTypes (data entities) in the Selling module:

- **Customer:** Stores customer details (name, contact info, customer type, credit limit, price list, etc.).
- **Quotation:** Key fields - customer, validity date, item lines (item, quantity, rate, amount), totals, and status. Quotation can reference a **Lead** (from CRM) before a customer is formally created.
- **Sales Order:** Key fields - customer, order date, required delivery date, item lines (with quantities and rates), taxes/charges, and a status (e.g. Draft/Submitted/Completed). Also flags like _"Is POS?"_ or _"Delivery Required"_.
- **Delivery Note:** Key fields - linked sales order, date, items (with actual delivered quantities, batch/serial numbers if applicable), delivery address, and status. Updates stock ledger when submitted.
- **Sales Invoice:** Key fields - customer, posting date, items (similar to order), taxes, payment terms, and status (Unpaid/Paid/Overdue). Invoice posts accounting entries (debit customer, credit income & tax).
- **Item:** (shared with Stock module) includes selling-related fields like selling rate, default sales UoM, and whether it can be sold.
- **Pricing Rule:** Defines conditions for discounts or special pricing (e.g. 5% off if quantity > 10 or for a certain customer group).
- **Campaign/Referral:** (If used) Could log marketing campaigns or referral programs tied to sales (to track lead sources, etc.).

**User Interface & Experience:** The Selling module is accessible through a dashboard and form views that are optimized for mobile. A sales user (or shop owner) can easily search and select items when making a quotation or order, with quick filters (by item group or by typing part of the name). The UI uses clear language - e.g., "New Sale" instead of "Sales Order" if targeting less tech-savvy users[\[17\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L80-L88)[\[18\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L294-L301). On mobile, forms are broken into collapsible sections or steps to avoid overwhelming the screen. For example, when creating a Sales Order on a phone, Step 1 could capture customer info (with an option to quickly add a new customer), Step 2 selects items (with a touch-friendly list of items and a search bar), and Step 3 confirms totals and tax. The module also provides a **Sales Dashboard** with key metrics like total sales this week, top-selling items, and outstanding receivables in a simple card format. Graphs or charts (e.g. a monthly sales trend) are shown as tappable images or sparklines for quick insight.

**Offline Capabilities:** Most **Selling** transactions can be initiated offline if needed. Specifically, the POS sub-module is built to work offline (see POS section), which covers a large portion of sales in a retail context. For other sales scenarios (like making a quotation or order for a bulk sale), offline use is less common but still supported: the app would allow creating a Quotation or Sales Order offline and mark it as "Pending Sync." The record would sync to the server when connectivity is restored, at which point any stock reservation or workflow actions are finalized. The system ensures no duplicate order numbers are issued by using a local temp ID that is reconciled on sync. While offline, the user will still be able to search for items and customers if those were cached - hence, the app caches the item catalog and recent customer list locally. Any price lists or tax templates should also be cached so that quotations/orders computed offline have correct pricing. **Note:** The Selling module's offline support is critical mainly for POS; for order management, it is a convenience that allows, say, a salesperson taking an order in the field without network to record it and sync later.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Naledi runs a small hardware store in a township. Using the Selling module, she records both over-the-counter sales and bulk orders from local contractors. For a walk-in customer buying a hammer and nails, she uses the POS interface on her tablet - even if her internet is down, the sale is recorded and a receipt is printed. Later, a local builder calls to inquire about cement prices. Naledi creates a_ _Quotation_ _in the system (on her phone) and sends it via WhatsApp. The builder accepts the quote, so she converts it to a_ _Sales Order_ _and schedules delivery. The system reserves the 100 bags of cement in inventory. When her driver delivers the goods, Naledi generates a_ _Delivery Note_ _from the app and captures the customer's signature. Finally, she issues a_ _Sales Invoice. All along, the system has been updating stock levels and accounting entries. That evening, TOSS's AI assistant sends Naledi a quick insight: "You sold 90% of your cement stock today - consider reordering soon."_

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The Selling module is enhanced by AI-driven features that act as a smart sales assistant. For example, the system can analyze past sales and customer behavior to suggest **"next best offers"** - if a customer frequently buys item A and B, the system might prompt the seller during quotation or checkout: "Customers who bought A often need C as well." It can also monitor sales trends and alert the business owner with friendly messages, like: "Sales are slower this week than last - consider a weekend promotion." The AI can automatically identify the **top customers** by revenue and prompt the owner to send them a thank-you message or a loyalty reward. It will watch pricing and margins too - if a salesperson tries to give a discount that pushes an item's margin below a threshold, the system can warn or require approval (or later notify the owner: "Discount on Order #123 was high, margin only 5%[\[19\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L234-L241)."). These insights and actions are integrated seamlessly into workflows (e.g., a pop-up suggestion in the order screen, or a daily sales summary via the dashboard). The goal is to augment the seller's decision-making, especially for users who may not have formal sales analysis training.

**Collaborative Network Features:** On the collaboration front, the Selling module enables township businesses to leverage group marketing and shared sales opportunities. For instance, **Referral Programs** could be network-wide: multiple spaza shops might participate in a referral scheme where customers referring new shoppers get a reward, and this is tracked across the network (e.g., if a customer refers someone to any shop in the network, all share the referral data). The module can also support **"group sales"** - for example, if a supplier offers a bulk deal that no single shop could afford, the system could allow a group of shops to collectively sell a bundle. Each shop would get a portion to sell, and the system monitors the overall campaign. Another collaborative scenario: shops sharing inventory info - a customer at Shop A wants an item that's out of stock there, the salesperson can check TOSS to see if a nearby Shop B (who agreed to data sharing) has it, then either redirect the customer or facilitate a transfer. The Selling module, tied with the Stock module, would handle the documentation of that transfer as an inter-company sale/purchase with minimal friction. All such collaborative sales activities respect permissions - businesses opt in to share certain data (like item availability) with trusted partners or the wider network.

## Buying (Procurement Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Buying module manages the procurement process end-to-end, helping businesses efficiently purchase goods and services and maintain healthy supplier relationships. It covers everything from requesting supplier quotes, placing purchase orders, receiving goods into stock, to handling supplier invoices. In essence, this module ensures that **stock is replenished** in a timely, controlled manner and that **purchases are tracked and optimized** for cost and quality[\[20\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=The%20Buying%20module%20in%20ERPNext,processes%20and%20optimise%20supplier%20relationships)[\[21\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment). For small businesses, this means simplifying tasks like reordering inventory and keeping tabs on what they owe suppliers.

**Core Workflows:** Key workflows in Buying include:

- **Material Request (Requisition):** Optionally, a department or shop can create a **Material Request** (indicating needed items and quantities). This is an internal document signaling procurement needs (e.g., a shop owner notes they need 50 units of product X). Material Requests can be consolidated or approved before ordering.
- **Request for Quotation (RFQ):** The system can generate RFQs to send to multiple suppliers for pricing, especially for new items or bulk buys[\[20\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=The%20Buying%20module%20in%20ERPNext,processes%20and%20optimise%20supplier%20relationships). Suppliers' quotes can be recorded for comparison.
- **Supplier Quotation:** Record any quotes received from suppliers (price lists, terms). This helps in selecting the best supplier for an order. For recurring items, the last purchase rate is auto-suggested or supplier price lists can be maintained.
- **Purchase Order (PO):** Create a **Purchase Order** to a chosen supplier for required items and quantities[\[22\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment). The PO outlines what is being purchased, at what price, and expected delivery date. POs can be directly made (if the supplier and item prices are known) or after RFQ/quotation process. Once a PO is submitted (confirmed), it often reserves budget and awaits receipt.
- **Purchase Receipt (Goods Receipt):** When ordered items arrive, record a **Purchase Receipt** (sometimes called Goods Received Note). Here the actual quantities received (which might be partial or have some discrepancy) are recorded, and stock levels are increased accordingly. Quality inspections may be triggered here (integration with Quality module if an item requires QC on receipt).
- **Purchase Invoice (Supplier Invoice):** Record the supplier's bill by creating a **Purchase Invoice**. This can be done upon receipt or later. The purchase invoice will reference the PO and/or receipt, include pricing, taxes, and any shipping or additional charges. Submitting a purchase invoice posts to accounting (accounts payable) and can update stock valuation.
- **Payments to Supplier:** Although handled in Accounting, the Buying module ties into tracking when and how supplier payments are made (either against the purchase invoice or as advance payments).
- **Stock Replenishment Workflow:** The module supports reordering rules - e.g., if stock for an item falls below a threshold, it can auto-generate a Material Request or even a draft Purchase Order for approval[\[23\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=The%20Stock%20or%20Inventory%20module,in%20ERPNext%20helps%20you%20to). This ties into the AI as well for suggestions.

**Business Rules & Validation:** Procurement must enforce certain rules:

- **Supplier Selection:** Only approved (active) suppliers can be used on POs. The system may enforce that for certain items, purchase must be from specific suppliers (if configured). If multiple quotes exist, selection should be justified (system can log which quotation was chosen for transparency).
- **PO Approval:** For larger orders or group buys, an approval step can be required (e.g., if order value > X, require manager approval). This can be configured via workflow.
- **Three-Way Matching:** The system supports matching PO -> Receipt -> Invoice. It validates that the quantities and prices on the purchase invoice do not exceed what was ordered and received beyond a tolerance. If a supplier invoice comes in with a higher rate or extra item, the system flags it for review. Likewise, if the received quantity is more than ordered, system either prevents over-receipt or logs it as excess (which could be returned or accepted as extra, depending on settings).
- **Stock Update:** A Purchase Receipt cannot be submitted if it would drive stock negative for returns or if mandatory batch/serial info is missing for items that require it. Submission of receipts and cancellations must update the stock ledger and **Stock module** accordingly in an atomic, consistent way.
- **Status Transitions:** PO statuses: Draft → Submitted (order placed) → Partially Received (if some items or partial quantities received) → Completed (fully received and invoiced) or Closed/Cancelled. Similar for Material Requests (open, approved, fulfilled) and others. The system automatically updates status (e.g., mark PO as "Completed" when linked receipts cover all quantities, and invoice is done).
- **Supplier Management:** The module maintains **Supplier** master records with contact info, payment terms, default currency, etc.[\[22\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment). It also can track a supplier's performance (like on-time delivery, quality issues) to inform future purchasing - this is more advanced, but even a simple rating or notes field is provided. Business rules could include blocking POs to blacklisted suppliers or warning if a supplier has pending issues.
- **Budget Control:** (If Accounting budgets are used) - warn or block if a purchase will cause an expense budget to exceed limits, relevant if the business sets spending budgets.

**Data Model & Key Fields:** Main DocTypes in Buying:

- **Supplier:** Stores supplier info (name, supplier type, default currency, credit terms, etc.). Also holds their bank details if needed for payments.
- **Material Request:** Key fields - requested items (with quantities), purpose (purchase vs internal transfer), required by date, and status. May include who requested it.
- **Supplier Quotation:** Key fields - supplier, items with quoted rates, validity. Often created from RFQ or entered manually.
- **Purchase Order:** Key fields - supplier, order date, expected delivery date, item table (item code, quantity, rate, amount, tax category), terms (like payment terms or incoterm), and status. Also links to project or cost center if purchases are for a specific project or department (for cost tracking).
- **Purchase Receipt:** Key fields - supplier, receiving date, reference PO, item table (received qty, rejected qty if any, batch/serial details), warehouse where stock is received, and status. Includes a checkbox if this receipt is to update stock (in some cases a "non-stock receipt" might be allowed for services, which doesn't affect stock).
- **Purchase Invoice:** Key fields - supplier, posting date, due date, item/services with amounts, taxes and charges (like VAT), and link to PO/receipt. Also includes bill reference number (supplier's invoice no.) for record. Payment status (Unpaid/Paid).
- **Item:** (from Stock module) has purchasing details like default supplier, last purchase rate, purchase UoM, etc.
- **Warehouse:** (from Stock) - needed when receiving items to stock.

Additionally, **Price List** and **Currency** are used if multi-currency purchasing is allowed (e.g., a shop might buy from an overseas supplier). The system should handle such, but township use likely local suppliers with local currency.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Buying module's UI is oriented towards simplicity - many small businesses don't have dedicated procurement officers, so the shop owner or manager will typically handle purchasing. The module provides a **"Reorder Items"** view or report that lists all items low in stock (with current level and suggested reorder qty) for quick action. With one tap, the user could add selected items to a new Purchase Order draft, making the reordering process very straightforward (especially on mobile). When creating a Purchase Order, the UI lets the user choose a supplier and then add items. On mobile, selecting items might be from a drop-down or a multi-select list of items that need restocking. The app might also allow scanning a product barcode to add it to the order (useful if reordering by scanning empty shelf items). Each item line can show last purchase price as a reference. The interface uses clear terms - e.g., "Buy from Supplier" for the PO form, "Goods Received" for the receipt form - instead of jargon.

For group buying scenarios, the UI might show a tag if an item can be bought as part of a group order (see Collaborative section). The Purchase Order list view highlights status (e.g., a partially received PO might show a progress bar of received vs ordered). **Notifications:** If any PO is overdue (expected date passed with no receipt), the system flags it and can notify the user ("Your order from Supplier X is overdue for 2 days").

Mobile offline behavior: while purchasing usually requires being online to communicate with suppliers, the app will allow creation of POs offline if needed (e.g., fill out what you need to buy in the field, sync later to actually send or export). However, critical functions like sending an RFQ email obviously need connectivity - the system will queue the email to send when back online.

**Offline Capabilities:** The Buying module benefits from offline mode primarily in terms of data access and drafting transactions. For instance, if a user is in a warehouse with no signal and doing a stock review, they might create a Material Request offline as they notice low items. The app will save it locally and sync it to the server when back online. The **item catalogue and supplier info** are cached so that even offline, the user can select items and suppliers on a PO. When network is available, the PO can be finalized and sent. Additionally, if multiple shops are on the platform under one tenant, a store manager might be offline but still record receipt of delivered goods - the Purchase Receipt can be made offline (so inventory on that device is updated locally) and then it syncs to update central stock when online. The system ensures that once synced, any pending accounting for receipts/invoices are posted properly. In case of conflicts (e.g., two offline users both try to receive the same PO), the server will reconcile by first-come-first-serve and notify if any duplicate or overlap happened.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Lerato owns a small spaza and needs to restock popular items like flour, sugar, and cold drinks. She checks her TOSS app's_ _Reorder Suggestions, which (based on low stock thresholds and recent sales) lists items to replenish. With one tap, she generates a_ _Purchase Order_ _for those items from her usual wholesaler. She's offline at the moment (no data coverage in the storeroom), but the app still lets her create the order. Later, when she gets connectivity, the PO syncs and she sends it out via email/WhatsApp to the supplier. A couple of days later, the supplier's truck arrives. Lerato opens the original PO on her phone and converts it to a_ _Purchase Receipt_ _by ticking off the items that were delivered. One item (sugar) comes short - she ordered 20 bags but only 15 arrived. She notes that in the receipt (the system will keep the PO open for the remaining 5). Instantly, her stock levels for sugar increase by 15 in the system_[_\[24\]_](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment)_. The next day, the supplier sends her an invoice for the delivered goods. She enters it as a_ _Purchase Invoice_ _in TOSS, which now shows she owes the supplier R5,000 payable in 30 days. The_ _AI assistant_ _in TOSS observes that multiple shops in her area also frequently reorder sugar around the same time; it suggests a_ _group buying opportunity_ _(covered later) so they could negotiate a bulk discount. It also notes the partial delivery and reminds Lerato to follow up on the 5 pending bags or adjust the order._

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Decision Support):** The Buying module is significantly enhanced by TOSS's intelligent layer. The AI monitors consumption rates and can generate **automated reorder suggestions**[\[25\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L222-L225)[\[26\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L500-L508). For example, it will learn seasonal patterns (e.g., cold drink sales spike in summer) and preemptively suggest higher reorder quantities ahead of time. It also keeps track of supplier performance - if a certain supplier's deliveries are often late or short, the system might alert the user or suggest an alternative supplier. When creating a Purchase Order, if similar businesses in the network are also looking to buy the same item, the AI might prompt: "3 other nearby shops also need sugar - consider a group purchase to save on costs." For cost control, the AI flags anomalies like "The price for flour in this PO is 10% higher than your last purchase[\[27\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L110-L115)" (prompting the user to possibly negotiate or check another supplier). The SaaS layer can also provide cash flow insight: before a user places a large order, it might warn if the bank balance is low or if many bills are due soon ("Reminder: You have R8,000 of supplier payments due next week[\[28\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L114-L117)"). These insights are delivered in a helpful tone, often via the module's UI (e.g., a warning icon next to a supplier name if there's a known issue, or a pop-up suggestion) and via summary notifications. Essentially, the AI acts as a purchasing advisor, helping small business owners make smarter buying decisions without needing a formal procurement department.

**Collaborative Network Features:** The Buying module opens up one of the most powerful collaborative features of TOSS: **Group Buying**. In a network of small businesses, TOSS can coordinate combined purchase orders. For example, ten spaza shops can aggregate their needs and place one large order to a wholesaler for bulk pricing. The system supports this by allowing a **"Multi-tenant Purchase Order"** or a mechanism where each shop creates a PO which the system then merges or links into a single **Group Order** for the supplier. The Collaborative layer manages permissions and data sharing: each participant sees the items and quantities they contributed, and perhaps the overall total, but not the others' sensitive info beyond what's necessary (like they might see "5 other shops are participating, total combined order = 100 units"). When the goods arrive, TOSS helps split the bulk delivery - generating individual Purchase Receipts for each shop's portion, while the primary receiver (maybe a hub) logs the main receipt. Financially, the system can either split the supplier invoice for each participant or record one invoice to a "group account" and track settlements from each shop. This requires trust, so the platform likely involves a **central facilitator** (could be a cooperative head or a nominated lead shop) who manages the transaction with the supplier. TOSS handles the communication: sending out a notice to the network "Opportunity: Bulk sugar at 10% off if 500kg total order. Pledge your quantity by Friday.", then consolidating responses.

Another collaborative aspect is **Vendor Management** in a shared sense. The module could allow sharing supplier ratings or experiences across the network (with consent). For instance, if one shop had issues with a supplier's product quality, they could flag it, and other shops see that note (like a community-driven supplier scorecard[\[29\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L426-L434)). Conversely, positive experiences or negotiation wins can be shared ("Supplier X gave us 5% off on bulk rice - mention that when you order"). The Buying module, through events, can also coordinate **shared logistics**: multiple shops can indicate they want to pick up from the supplier's depot, so the system triggers a combined pickup plan (in conjunction with the Logistics/Supply Chain module). All these scenarios require event-driven communication and permissioned data sharing, which the Collaborative Network layer provides (detailed later). In summary, the Buying module is not just about one business purchasing, but enabling many small buyers to act collectively as a bigger buyer for better pricing and efficiency[\[30\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L274-L282).

## CRM (Customer Relationship Management)

**Overview & Purpose:** The CRM module focuses on managing leads, customer interactions, and sales opportunities, serving as the pre-sales and client relationship hub that feeds into the Selling module. It enables businesses to **capture leads, follow up proactively, and nurture customer relationships** in an organized way[\[13\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/CRM#:~:text=The%20CRM%20module%20in%20ERPNext,interactions%20and%20streamline%20sales%20processes). For township and rural businesses, CRM might include keeping track of regular customers' preferences, managing informal customer credit, and simple loyalty mechanisms. The goal is to enhance customer service and not let any sales opportunity slip through the cracks.

**Core Workflows:** Key processes in CRM include:

- **Lead Management:** Record new **Leads** (potential customers or inquiries). A lead entry typically includes name, contact info, how they heard about the business, and what they're interested in. For example, a walk-in who asks for a product currently out of stock can be noted as a lead to call back when stock arrives. Leads can be captured via an online form (if using the website), via WhatsApp inquiries, or manually by staff[\[31\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/CRM#:~:text=,to%20ensure%20effective%20customer%20engagement).
- **Lead Nurturing & Communication:** Schedule follow-ups for leads. The system can create **To-Do** or **Events** (calls/meetings) linked to leads - e.g., "Call John next Monday about catering quote." Keep a log of communications (calls made, emails sent, meetings). If the business uses integrated messaging (email/SMS/WhatsApp), those messages can be logged under the lead or customer.
- **Opportunity Tracking:** Convert qualified leads into **Opportunities** (a potential sale with more defined requirements)[\[31\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/CRM#:~:text=,to%20ensure%20effective%20customer%20engagement). For instance, if a lead expresses serious interest in a bulk order, an Opportunity is recorded with expected deal size and probability of closing. Opportunities can have stages (Prospecting → Quotation Sent → Negotiation → Won/Lost).
- **Quotation and Pipeline Integration:** From an Opportunity, users can directly create a **Quotation** in the Selling module. The CRM pipeline view shows all open opportunities and their stages, giving a visual of the sales funnel (e.g., how many deals are likely this month). In a small business context, this might be a simple list with color codes for stage.
- **Customer Conversion:** When a lead or opportunity is "won" (customer decides to buy), the system can convert that lead into a formal **Customer** record (if not already) and link any successful Opportunity to the resulting Sales Order (in Selling module). This provides traceability from initial contact to actual sale.
- **Activity Management:** Manage tasks, calls, and meetings. The CRM module often includes a calendar or task list view of all upcoming customer-related activities[\[32\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/CRM#:~:text=information%2C%20transaction%20history%2C%20and%20communication,customer%20behavior%2C%20and%20CRM%20effectiveness). For example, "Visit Shoprite distributor on 5th Dec" could be an event in the system. This ensures commitments to customers or prospects are not forgotten.
- **Loyalty and Customer Feedback (if applicable):** In a more advanced scenario, CRM can handle loyalty program data (points, tiers) and store customer feedback or support issues (overlap with Support module). For an MVP, a simple notes field or tagging important customers ("VIP") might suffice.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Lead Deduplication:** The system should help avoid duplicate leads/customers. If someone enters a new lead with an email or phone that matches an existing customer, it should alert or auto-link to the existing record to maintain one profile per person/company.
- **Follow-up Discipline:** If a next follow-up date is set for a lead or opportunity, the system could enforce that a new date must be set when completing the current follow-up, preventing "orphaned" leads with no next action. This ensures continuous engagement until closed or lost.
- **Opportunity Stage Progression:** Not strictly enforced, but generally an opportunity should not skip stages without reason (the system might log a change in probability or expected closing date so managers/owners can see if things are accelerating or stalled).
- **Customer Credit Tracking:** A simplified CRM in a township context might incorporate **informal credit** tracking - e.g., if a loyal customer buys on credit, the amount owed could be recorded in their profile (or via Accounts). Business rule: a customer owing beyond a certain amount could trigger a warning on new sales (tying back into Selling validations).
- **Data Privacy:** By POPIA compliance, personal info of leads/customers (names, contacts) should be protected. The system will ensure only authorized users can see full contact details, and that there's consent for things like promotional messages. If a lead opts out of communications, mark them as such and exclude from bulk SMS, etc.

**Data Model & Key Fields:** Main entities in CRM:

- **Lead:** Fields for lead name (or organization), contact info (phone, email), source of lead (referral, walk-in, social media, etc.), and a status (Open, Contacted, Converted, Do Not Contact). It may also have a field for interested products or notes on inquiry.
- **Opportunity:** Fields include linked customer/lead, opportunity type (sale, project, etc.), items or services of interest (sometimes a child table listing what they want, with estimated amounts), expected closing date, stage, probability (% chance to win), and an expected value (which could be auto-calculated or entered). Also an owner (salesperson responsible).
- **Contact & Address:** Master data for contacts and addresses, which can link to customers or suppliers. A lead might auto-create a Contact record when converted. Key fields: phone numbers, email, and address lines.
- **Customer (from Selling module):** Once a lead is converted, the Customer record holds long-term info like credit limit, loyalty points (if any), etc., and is used for actual transactions.
- **Communication Log:** A timeline of communications (this might be a unified doctype capturing any emails, call notes, etc. linked to Lead/Opportunity/Customer). Fields: date, medium (call, email), summary, and reference link.
- **ToDo/Reminder:** A simple doctype for tasks or follow-ups. Fields: description, due date, linked to (could be a lead or opportunity), assigned to user.

**User Interface & Experience:** The CRM interface should present a **"Customer Pipeline"** view that's easy to scan on mobile. This could be a kanban board of opportunities by stage, or simply grouped lists: New Leads, In Progress, Won, Lost. On a small phone screen, likely a list with badges for stage might be better. Each lead or opportunity entry in the list shows key info (name, deal amount or interest, and next follow-up date). Tapping it opens a detail page where the user can scroll through contact info, notes, past communications, and quick actions like "Call" or "Send SMS" (which if tapped, can integrate with phone's dialer or WhatsApp). A big **"Convert to Sale"** button could be present when a deal is won, which then guides the user to create a Sales Order or Invoice in the Selling module.

The CRM module also provides a unified view of a customer's profile: even for existing customers (not just leads), the business owner can view their purchase history, any outstanding amounts (pulled from Accounting), and any open support tickets (from Support module). This 360° view helps in providing personalized service. The UI should keep things simple: for example, an **"Add Lead"** form with minimal fields (perhaps name and phone are all that's mandatory to start, the rest optional). The system can fill some info automatically - e.g., if a lead comes via the website inquiry form, it appears in CRM with source "Website" and relevant details pre-filled.

Mobile notifications are crucial: the app should remind the user each morning of any follow-ups due that day ("You have 2 follow-ups: Call Thabo, Meet with Dineo"). It should also alert when a lead has been idle too long or an opportunity is near its expected close date without an update.

**Offline Capabilities:** CRM activities revolve around communication, which often assumes connectivity. However, TOSS CRM still offers offline support for data entry and viewing. A user can access their lead and customer lists offline if those were previously synced. This means while on the road with poor signal, a salesperson can pull up a customer's phone number from the app (since contacts are cached) and make a call. They can also log call notes or create a new lead offline. These entries will be time-stamped and saved locally, then sync to the server when back online. If an appointment or follow-up was completed offline, the system syncs the update (so colleagues, if any, can see it's done). One limitation offline is sending emails or messages - those will queue. For instance, if a user writes an email reply to a lead in the CRM interface offline, the email will be sent out once connectivity returns (the system should make this seamless with a queued outbox). This ensures that even with spotty networks, the user can keep working - jotting down new prospect info or updating statuses - without losing information, and the data will reconcile with the central server later.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Tebogo runs a small catering business. She meets a potential client at a community event who is interested in a large order for a wedding next month. Using the TOSS CRM module on her phone, Tebogo quickly adds a_ _Lead: "Naledi Mokgoko - wedding catering for 200 guests, event on Jan 15". She enters Naledi's phone number and sets a follow-up for next week to discuss menu and pricing. Back at the shop, Tebogo elaborates this entry into an_ _Opportunity_ _with an estimated value and probability. Over the next few days, she uses the CRM to log communications: Naledi prefers SMS, so Tebogo's replies via WhatsApp Web are noted in the system (she copies key points into a comment on the opportunity). The system prompts Tebogo with a task: "Send quotation by Friday". Tebogo creates a_ _Quotation_ _(via Selling module) directly from the Opportunity, selecting menu packages. Naledi confirms the quote, so Tebogo marks the Opportunity as_ _Won_ _and converts Naledi into a Customer in the system. A_ _Sales Order_ _is generated for the event. Throughout, the CRM kept Tebogo on track - even reminding her to ask for feedback after the event. She also uses CRM to track her regular lunch customers: she notes who her top 10 repeat customers are and their preferences (extra spicy, vegetarian, etc.) in the Customer records. Now, when any of those customers call, she has their history at her fingertips and can greet them by name, building loyalty._

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** AI in the CRM module serves as a virtual sales assistant and customer analyst. For example, the AI can rank leads by likelihood to convert, based on factors like response time or similarity to past successful leads (e.g., "This lead is similar to your best customer profile"). It might highlight dormant leads: "You haven't contacted Thabo in 3 weeks, and he was interested in a big order - consider reaching out again." For opportunities, the AI can forecast which deals might close this month by analyzing pipeline and past conversion rates[\[33\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/CRM#:~:text=stages%20of%20the%20sales%20funnel,and%20ensure%20accurate%20order%20fulfillment). It can also watch engagement: if a lead hasn't responded to two messages, the AI might suggest a different approach or offer ("Lead Sam hasn't replied - maybe offer a small first-time discount to entice him"). Another insight is **customer segmentation** - the AI can categorize customers (e.g., big spenders, frequent small buyers, seasonal customers) and prompt targeted actions. In a rural context, this could be as simple as "Your top 5 customers drove 40% of sales - perhaps reward them with a thank you or bonus." If integrated with social media or WhatsApp, AI could help draft friendly broadcast messages for promotions, tuned to the local tone and language.

Moreover, the AI ties CRM with other modules: It knows which customers owe money (from Accounting) and can caution before new sales ("Note: This customer has an outstanding balance of R500" - credit control). It also knows stock levels and can avoid missed opportunities: if a lead asked for an item that was out of stock, once that item is restocked, the system reminds the user to inform the interested leads. Essentially, the AI ensures no opportunity is forgotten and every customer feels attended to, acting as a smart CRM coach.

**Collaborative Network Features:** CRM is inherently about relationships, and the collaborative aspect in TOSS can extend to community-wide customer engagement. One scenario is **shared leads or referrals** among businesses. For instance, if one business gets a query for something they don't offer, they can forward that lead to another trusted business on the platform (with the lead's permission). TOSS could facilitate this by allowing a lead to be shared as an opportunity to another tenant, logging the referral. This could be common in a cooperative or business network: a hardware shop might refer a construction project lead to a bricks supplier, or a salon might refer a customer looking for a product to a neighboring general dealer. The system can track referrals and even automate a small referral incentive if applicable ("Refer a customer to any network shop and earn points").

Another network angle: **Community loyalty program.** Multiple small businesses could unite under a single loyalty program (e.g., a township "Buy Local Rewards" card). TOSS CRM would then handle points that are accumulated across different shops. This requires sharing a customer's identity (with consent) across tenants. For example, a customer registers once, and whenever they shop at any participating store, the sale is recorded towards their loyalty points. The CRM module in each tenant's app would identify the customer (perhaps via phone number or a QR code on a card) and update the central loyalty ledger. This fosters customer retention within the network - a customer is encouraged to patronize any shop in the TOSS network to maximize their rewards. The CRM module and Network layer would jointly manage the rules (points per rand spent, tier levels) and redemptions (maybe a standardized reward catalog or store-specific offers).

Privacy and trust are paramount - by default, each business sees only their own customer data. If the network implements a shared program, customers would explicitly opt-in, and their basic profile might be visible to participating stores (possibly through a secure lookup service rather than a full data share). Event-driven triggers would handle things like "Customer reached 1000 points - notify them of a reward" across the network.

In summary, CRM's collaborative aspect in TOSS is about **referral sharing** and **joint customer engagement initiatives** that individual micro-businesses alone might struggle to maintain, but together they can, strengthening the local business ecosystem.

## Stock (Inventory Management Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Stock (Inventory) module enables businesses to **track and control their inventory** of products and materials across one or multiple locations. It covers maintaining item details, recording stock movements (incoming and outgoing), and providing real-time stock levels and valuations[\[23\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=The%20Stock%20or%20Inventory%20module,in%20ERPNext%20helps%20you%20to). This ensures that small businesses know exactly what they have in stock, what's running low, and where their goods are. Given the offline, rural context, the Stock module is designed to be simple to use (no complicated warehouse jargon) while robust enough to prevent losses due to stockouts, expiries, or shrinkage.

**Core Workflows:** Key processes in the Stock module include:

- **Item Master Management:** Define all **Items** (products, raw materials, supplies) in the system with unique codes and essential attributes (unit of measure, default selling/purchasing rates, whether it's tracked in stock, etc.). For example, a 500g bread loaf is an item with perhaps a SKU code.
- **Stock In** (Inbound Movements): These can happen via:
- **Purchase Receipts:** When goods are bought and received (from the Buying module), stock levels increase in the designated Warehouse.
- **Stock Entries (Material Receipt):** Direct adjustments, e.g., if opening balance stock is recorded or if stock is donated/free. Also used for production (finished goods coming in from manufacturing).
- **Returns In:** Sales returns add items back to stock.
- **Stock Out** (Outbound Movements): These include:
- **Delivery Notes / Sales Invoices:** Selling an item reduces its stock in the warehouse.
- **Stock Entries (Material Issue):** For recording waste, damage, or other write-offs (e.g., expired goods thrown away).
- **Returns Out:** If returning goods to a supplier, reducing stock.
- **Stock Transfers:** Move stock between **Warehouses** (locations). E.g., from main storage to shop front, or between branches. A Stock Entry of type "Transfer" handles this. For multi-location businesses or future hub-and-spoke operations, this is important.
- **Stock Reconciliation (Stock Take):** Periodically (or continuously) allow counting physical stock and reconciling with system. A **Stock Reconciliation** document can be used to adjust the system's quantities to match actual counts, posting any discrepancies to an accounting difference account.
- **Batch & Serial Management:** If enabled for certain items (like medicines with batch numbers or appliances with serial numbers), the module supports tracking by batch (with expiry dates) or serial (unique item IDs). This includes selecting specific batch/serial on stock transactions and ensuring their availability.
- **Valuation & Ledger:** Maintain a **Stock Ledger** and **Stock Balance** for each item, recording every quantity change with timestamp and reference document[\[34\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=The%20Stock%20or%20Inventory%20module,in%20ERPNext%20helps%20you%20to). Also maintain stock valuation (using methods like FIFO or moving average) to know the inventory value for accounting.
- **Reports & Alerts:** Provide reports like Current Stock Levels, Stock Ledger (history of movements), Stock Aging (how long items have stayed unsold), and Low Stock Report. Alerts for low stock are generated if items drop below their re-order level.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **No Negative Stock (Configurable):** By default, the system should prevent issuing stock if not enough quantity is available. For example, you cannot deliver 10 units if only 5 are in stock (unless a setting to allow negative stock is turned on for flexibility, but then an alert is raised). This ensures stock figures don't go unrealistically negative and catches potential mistakes.
- **Warehouse Mandatory:** All stock transactions must specify a **Warehouse** (even if a small business has only one stock location, a default "Main Store" warehouse is used). This helps future expansion (multiple shops or storage areas) and ensures location tracking. The system validates that the warehouse exists and the item is allowed there (items might be stored in all warehouses by default).
- **Batch/Serial Integrity:** If an item is batch-managed, any outgoing transaction must specify a valid batch that exists with sufficient quantity. Similarly for serial-managed items, each serial number can only be in one place at a time, and once sold or removed, it cannot be picked again unless returned. The system enforces unique serial numbers and tracks their status (available, sold, etc.).
- **Valuation Consistency:** Transactions affecting stock value (buying, selling, adjustments) create corresponding accounting entries (stock asset debits/credits) in the background. The system ensures the total valuation in accounting matches the stock ledger valuation for each item. If not (due to manual journal or error), it flags a reconciliation needed.
- **FIFO for Expiry:** For perishable goods, the system should support **First-Expiring-First-Out** logic. While not strictly enforced without batch metadata, if batches have expiry dates, it can warn users to sell or use those expiring soon first. Business rule: do not allow issuing expired stock (the system can warn or block if the batch date is past).
- **Stock Lock Period:** Optionally, a business might lock older stock entries after accounts are finalized (e.g., no adjustments in a closed month). If a user tries to post a back-dated stock entry in a locked period, it should be prevented.
- **Auto-Reorder Triggers:** When stock goes below reorder level, the system marks that item as "To Reorder". This can trigger creation of Material Requests or notifications (as described in Buying). The business rule is that reorder suggestion should only fire if there isn't already an open PO or if last reorder hasn't arrived, to avoid duplication (i.e., consider on-order quantities).
- **Unit of Measure (UOM) Consistency:** If multiple UOMs are used (like selling by unit but stocking by box), proper conversion factors must be defined. The system ensures that any stock transaction is converted to the base stock UOM for accounting and quantity tracking.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Item:** Central master with fields: Item Code, Item Name, Item Group (category), default UOM, whether it is Stock Item, Opening Stock quantity (for initial load), valuation method, standard buying/selling rates, reorder level and reorder quantity (per warehouse), and flags for batch/serial tracking.
- **Warehouse:** Master for locations (could be a physical location or virtual grouping). Fields: Warehouse Name, Parent (for hierarchy, e.g., Region > Site > Section), and possibly capacity info. For small use, likely just a flat list (e.g., "Store Room", "Shop Front").
- **Stock Ledger Entry:** Each stock move creates entries here (not usually directly viewed by users except in reports). Fields: Item, Warehouse, Date/Time, Voucher Type (e.g., Delivery Note), Voucher No., Qty In/Out, Balance Qty after, and Value change.
- **Stock Balance (computed):** Not a doctype, but the system maintains running totals per item per warehouse.
- **Stock Entry:** A document used for various internal stock movements or adjustments. Fields: Purpose (Material Issue, Receipt, Transfer, Reconciliation, Manufacture, etc.), From/To Warehouse, Item lines (item, qty, source and target warehouse for transfers, and optionally an expense account for write-off).
- **Batch:** If used, fields: Item, Batch ID, Manufacture/Expiry dates, quantity currently in stock (system maintained).
- **Serial No:** Fields: Serial Number, Item, purchase and sale info (if sold, to whom, when), current Warehouse (or status like "Delivered").
- **UOM and UOM Conversion:** Master of Units of Measure and mapping (e.g., 1 Case = 12 Each) if needed.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Stock module should present an **Inventory Dashboard** at a glance: e.g., total stock value on hand, number of items in stock, and alerts like "5 items below re-order level"[\[26\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L500-L508). On mobile, this might be a simple list of those alerts and a searchable list of items. The **Item list** view shows each item's available quantity (possibly only for a default warehouse unless expanded). Tapping an item shows its **Item Card**: including a photo (if uploaded), description, current stock in each warehouse, reorder level, recent transactions (last 5 movements or so), and maybe a quick action to "Adjust Stock" or "Reorder".

Performing a stock transaction (like an adjustment) is made easy: e.g., to record wastage of an item, a user can go to that Item's page and hit "Adjust Stock" - the app then asks "How many did you remove from stock and why?" with a simple interface (e.g., "Quantity: 2, Reason: Expired" and it creates a Stock Entry for Material Issue behind the scenes to reduce stock). This is crucial for non-technical users so they don't need to navigate accounting or journal entries - just a straightforward question-and-answer flow.

For stock counts, the UI could have a **Stock Take mode**: generate a checklist of items to count (maybe filter by warehouse or category), input counted numbers, and then finalize adjustments. Possibly allow printing or exporting a count sheet if done on paper then input results.

The mobile UI uses clear terms: "Stock" for inventory, "Add Stock" or "Remove Stock" rather than technical terms. In low-connectivity scenarios, heavy data like item images can be deferred unless requested, to keep the app responsive.

**Offline Capabilities:** The Stock module must work robustly offline because stock operations might be done in back rooms or warehouses without internet. The app will cache the **item master** and current stock levels so that even offline, a user can see what they **think** should be on the shelf as per system. They can then do a count and input adjustments offline. All types of stock entries (receipts, issues, transfers) can be initiated offline. The data (with timestamps) will sync later. The system uses local storage to queue up transactions, and each is applied in order once online, with conflict resolution if needed. For example, two offline adjustments on the same item: when syncing, they'll apply sequentially as recorded.

One complexity offline is **stock reservations** (like for Sales Orders) - but the system design likely keeps critical reservation logic server-side to avoid conflict. So, if offline POS sales are happening, they will sync and reduce stock; the system might accept temporary negative stock until synchronization resolves actual sequence of events (especially if multiple devices selling the same item offline). The platform addresses this by making stock transactions idempotent and reconciled via timestamps or a central queue on sync[\[35\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L316-L324). If any discrepancy arises (e.g., stock went negative or two sales claim the last item), the system generates an alert for manual reconciliation. However, such cases are minimized by providing the latest known stock info to each device before going offline and possibly locking certain operations if clearly not feasible (for instance, if a user tries to transfer stock offline from a warehouse that was at zero, the app should warn them).

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Ayanda manages a community pharmacy. In her stock room, network is unreliable. She uses TOSS Stock module on a tablet to do a weekly inventory check. The app, even offline, shows her current expected quantities. She notices some discrepancies: e.g., for Paracetamol tablets, system says 100 packs, but she counts 95. She enters an adjustment (5 units lost due to damage or theft). For certain medicines, she tracks batch and expiry - one batch of vitamins is expiring next month. The system had already alerted her a month ago about this ("Batch #VIT100 will expire in 30 days"), so she ran a promotion to sell them faster. During stock take, she finds only 2 bottles left of that batch, which she removes from display. She records in TOSS a_ _Material Issue_ _of 2 units with reason "Expired". All these changes are done offline in the storeroom. Later, when she goes to the front of the shop with connectivity, the tablet syncs: stock levels update on the central server, and accounting entries for the write-offs are posted automatically. Meanwhile, throughout the week, every sale made via the POS also decreased stock in real-time (or near real-time if offline). Ayanda uses the Low Stock Report to see that certain fast-moving items (cough syrup, sanitizer) are below their reorder levels_[_\[36\]_](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=,time%20information%20via%20reports)_. She quickly creates a Purchase Order for those via the Buying module. TOSS's AI notices a trend that cough syrup sells faster during the winter season and suggests that Ayanda should maintain a higher minimum level for winter months._

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The AI layer supercharges the Stock module by acting as an inventory analyst for the business. Key AI-driven features include **reorder suggestions and stock alerts**: the system doesn't just use static reorder levels, but dynamically adjusts recommendations based on recent sales velocity and upcoming events[\[25\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L222-L225)[\[37\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L510-L514). For example, if an item's sales have spiked due to a flu outbreak, the AI will suggest ordering more before the usual threshold. It might say, "You usually reorder at 10 units remaining, but 10 sold in the last 2 days - increase your reorder quantity or you'll run out." The AI also flags **dead stock** - items that haven't sold in a long time. It could gently remind: "Item X hasn't sold in 60 days. Consider a discount or promotion to clear it." or suggest returning it to supplier if possible.

For perishable goods, the AI monitors expiry dates and proactively warns: "5 bottles of milk will expire next week[\[37\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L510-L514). Propose a discount to sell them in time." If integrated with the POS, it might even prompt the cashier to upsell those expiring items at a discount. The AI also keeps an eye on **stock valuation and shrinkage**. If the system sees frequent stock adjustments for losses, it surfaces that pattern: "Stock adjustments for Item Y have occurred 3 times this month, totaling R500 - potential theft or spoilage issue." This helps the owner catch problems early.

Another insight: **optimal stock levels** and **storage costs**. The AI can learn seasonal patterns and suggest changes in reorder levels: e.g., "It's rainy season - demand for umbrellas rises. Keep at least 20 in stock instead of 5." Conversely, "Demand for cold drinks drops in winter - lower your reorder level to save cash." These suggestions mimic an experienced inventory planner guiding a novice business owner.

Additionally, for multi-warehouse setups (or later, a central depot plus shops), the AI assists in **stock redistribution**. For example, if one branch has surplus of an item and another has shortage, it can recommend a transfer: "Shop A has 30 units of maize meal (10 above optimal), Shop B is out of stock - consider transferring 10 units from A to B." In a collaborative sense, this extends to the network: if Ayanda has excess of something nearing expiry, the AI might alert nearby shops in the network that could take some off her hands (better than it expiring - covered in Network section).

**Collaborative Network Features:** Inventory is an area ripe for collaboration in TOSS. One major feature is **Shared Inventory Visibility** for network participants who opt in. For example, a group of independent shops in the same area may agree to make certain stock info visible to each other (perhaps just quantity available of key items). The Stock module, via the network layer, could then show that "Neighbors have X in stock" for an item. This enables a few collaborative scenarios:

- **Cross-store Fulfillment:** If Shop A runs out of an item but Shop B (nearby) has it, Shop A can quickly arrange to get it from B (either by purchasing at cost or borrowing and returning later). TOSS can facilitate generating the necessary documents: a stock transfer or an inter-company sale/purchase. This helps prevent lost sales due to stockouts and fosters a supportive network.
- **Group Stock Monitoring:** A wholesaler or supplier on the platform (if included as a tenant or connected system) might monitor the stock levels of all connected shops for their products (with permission) to proactively plan deliveries (Vendor Managed Inventory concept). For example, a beverage supplier could see when each shop's soda stock is low and preemptively send a refill truck - improving efficiency for both supplier and shop. The Stock module would publish low-stock events to such partners if configured.
- **Shared Warehouse or Depot:** In some communities, businesses could co-own a storage facility for bulk goods. TOSS can manage that by treating the depot as a separate tenant or a shared warehouse where each business has an allocated section (or share). The collaborative aspect is that multiple businesses' stock might physically reside together. The system would carefully segregate ownership in records but allow a combined view for the depot manager. Events like group purchases delivered to the shared depot are split into each owner's stock via the system (like a distribution).
- **Pooling for Insurance / Financing:** Knowing the total inventory value across the network could enable group insurance or collateral for loans. While not directly a Stock module feature, the data from Stock feeds into such network-level initiatives. E.g., "All shops together have R500k of inventory; use this as collateral for a group credit line." TOSS could produce a combined inventory report (with consent) for a lender or insurer, an example of cross-tenant reporting.

Permissions and data isolation are crucial. The default is no one sees another's stock. Any sharing is opt-in at a granular level (maybe per item or category, and whether exact quantities or just "in/out of stock" status). The Collaborative layer triggers - e.g., low stock alerts can be optionally broadcast: a shop could flag an alert "I need 20 units of Item Z, anyone have excess?" which others receive and can respond to. Underneath, if they agree, the system converts it to a formal transfer request.

In short, the Stock module in a network context helps the community act like a virtual co-op: sharing surplus, jointly avoiding stockouts, and aggregating their inventory information for mutual benefit (like bulk buying and shared storage). This kind of coordination, traditionally difficult for disparate small entities, is made possible through the real-time data and event sharing that TOSS enables[\[37\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L510-L514).

## Accounting (Finance Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Accounting module handles the financial backbone of the platform, recording all **money in and money out** so business owners can see their financial health at a glance. It covers bookkeeping tasks such as invoicing, payments, expenses, and financial reports (income statement, balance sheet) - but TOSS presents these in a simplified, jargon-free manner suitable for non-accountants[\[38\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L202-L208). The purpose is to ensure every transaction in other modules (sales, purchases, payroll, etc.) reflects in the books automatically, giving an accurate picture of cash flow and profitability without requiring the user to be a finance expert.

**Core Workflows:** Key accounting processes include:

- **Sales and Accounts Receivable:** Every **Sales Invoice** (from Selling module) flows into accounting, logging income and if on credit, an accounts receivable entry for the customer[\[39\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/accounts#:~:text=In%20ERPNext%2C%20accounting%20operations%20consists,of%203%20main%20transactions). Users can record **Payments Received** against customer invoices (or as advance payments). If a customer buys on credit (informal 'book'), the system tracks that outstanding amount under their name.
- **Purchases and Accounts Payable:** Every **Purchase Invoice** (from Buying module) logs an expense and accounts payable to the supplier[\[39\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/accounts#:~:text=In%20ERPNext%2C%20accounting%20operations%20consists,of%203%20main%20transactions). Users record **Payments Made** to suppliers, which settle those liabilities. The system can manage partial payments or prepayments and adjust accordingly.
- **Expense Tracking (Petty Cash):** The business can record expenses that are not through a supplier invoice - e.g., cash expenses like fuel, minor equipment, or staff lunch. This could be via a **Payment Entry** coded to an expense account or a simplified **Expense Voucher** form. TOSS will allow quick logging of such outflows to keep the "What's left" accurate.
- **Cash Management:** The module monitors cash/bank balances. **Cash Register/POS closing** is part of this: at day's end, tally cash collected from sales versus system-calculated cash, then create an entry if there's over/short. Bank deposits or withdrawals can be recorded too.
- **General Journal & Adjustments:** For completeness, accountants can pass **Journal Entries** (e.g., to record depreciation, corrections, or owner drawings). This is advanced usage; the UI for normal users might hide this, but it's available under the hood or for accountants' access.
- **Payroll Entries:** Integration from HR - salary payouts are recorded (e.g., via a journal entry or expense entry posting to salaries expense and reducing cash/bank).
- **Financial Reporting:** The system generates basic reports: **Profit & Loss (Income Statement)**, **Balance Sheet**, and **Cash Flow**. For user-friendliness, these are phrased in simple terms (Income vs. Expenses, Assets vs. Liabilities). Also, a **Trial Balance** and **General Ledger** report for accountants. On the dashboard, a simplified view "Money In / Money Out / What's Left" is shown, which essentially is cash flow: money received this month, money spent, and net remaining[\[38\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L202-L208).
- **Tax Management:** If the business is VAT registered or has any tax obligations, the module helps accumulate tax from sales and purchases (input VAT, output VAT) for filing. For very small informal businesses, this might be disabled, but for those in formal sector, it's important. TOSS can produce a tax report if needed (aligning with local tax like South African VAT requirements[\[40\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/accounts#:~:text=Introduction)).

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Double-Entry Integrity:** The module enforces that every financial transaction is balanced (debits = credits). Users typically won't see debits/credits, as forms abstract it (e.g., on a Payment form they just pick from which account to pay and which invoice to settle, system does the rest). But under the hood, if anything unbalanced is attempted, it will error - ensuring accounts always remain consistent.
- **Period Closure:** Optionally, monthly or yearly books can be "closed" to prevent backdated entries that alter past numbers. If March is closed, you can't book something into March anymore, only April onward, unless you have permission and reopen.
- **Unique Invoice Numbering:** Sales and Purchase Invoices likely need unique numbering (and maybe sequential, as per some regulations). The system auto-generates these, but ensures no duplicates and maintains sequence (especially if multiple offline invoices sync, it might assign numbers on sync to keep sequence).
- **Negative Accounting Entries Prevention:** E.g., you shouldn't create a payment entry for more money than the invoice amount (no overpayment without credit note logic), or a credit note exceeding original invoice. The system validates such conditions.
- **Currency Handling:** If multi-currency transactions occur (like buying from a supplier in USD), the system manages conversion rates and gains/losses. The rule is each invoice has a defined currency and rate, and the base (company) currency is always updated. Exchange rate fields must be filled and consistent.
- **Tax Compliance:** If taxes are applied, relevant fields (tax amount, tax type) must be present. The system can enforce tax inclusive/exclusive consistency. Also, if a customer or supplier is tax-exempt, it must be flagged so invoices don't charge incorrectly.
- **AR/AP Aging:** Keep track of credit periods. If a customer's invoice goes beyond due date unpaid, system flags it (for follow-up). Similarly for supplier payments. Possibly a simple rule: highlight any invoice over e.g. 30 days due as overdue.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Chart of Accounts (COA):** A hierarchical list of accounts (Assets, Liabilities, Equity, Income, Expenses). TOSS would provide a default simple COA suitable for small retail (with accounts like Cash, Bank, Inventory, Accounts Receivable/Payable, Sales, Purchases, Expenses, etc.). Each transaction posts to relevant accounts. Key fields: account name, type, balance.
- **Sales Invoice:** Fields - customer, date, due date, item lines (each posting to income and maybe tax accounts), totals, and posting status. Flags for credit note or returns.
- **Purchase Invoice:** Fields - supplier, date, due date, items/expenses lines (posting to expense or stock accounts), taxes, and payment status.
- **Payment Entry:** A document for recording payment. Fields - party type (Customer/Supplier), party name, date, amount, mode of payment (cash, bank, mobile money), accounts (from which account to which). It can have references to one or multiple invoices it settles.
- **Journal Entry:** Fields - date, remarks, a table of entries (Account, Debit amount, Credit amount). Used for adjustments not covered by dedicated forms.
- **Expense Claim/Voucher (if separate):** Possibly a simpler form for internal expenses. Fields - expense type, amount, date, paid by whom or to whom.
- **GL Entry:** The behind-the-scenes record for every debit/credit. Fields - account, date, voucher type and ID (linking to invoice, etc.), debit amount, credit amount, balance. Used for ledger reports.
- **Company:** Master record for the business's details (currency, financial year start, default accounts, etc. - though in multi-tenant each tenant has their own).
- **Fiscal Year:** If needed, defines financial year periods.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Accounting UI in TOSS aims to demystify accounting. It likely features a **Finance Dashboard** with three big numbers: Money In, Money Out, and Cash Balance (or Profit)[\[38\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L202-L208). For example, "This Month: Sales R10,000 - Expenses R7,000 - What's Left R3,000" in bold, friendly format. It may also show counters like "Unpaid Customer Invoices: 2 (total R1,200)" and "Upcoming Bills: 1 (R500 due next week)".

The navigation avoids accounting terms where possible: instead of "General Ledger", say "All Transactions" or simply present the detail when needed. There could be a toggle for "Simple view" vs "Advanced view". In simple view (default for most users), you see invoices, payments, and expenses in plain language. For example, to record an expense, the UI might literally have a button "Record an Expense" - clicking it presents a form: "What did you pay for? \[text or choose category\], How much? \[amount\], When? \[date\], How did you pay? \[cash/bank\]". The system behind will pick the right accounts (like debit an expense account, credit cash/bank) without the user choosing from the chart of accounts. Categories could map to accounts (e.g., "Transport" goes to Travel Expense account).

Similarly, receiving money (aside from sales via invoices) can be "Record Other Income" if needed. But for most, sales and purchase modules feed in so they don't manually create incomes or COGS entries.

For users with knowledge or accountants, an advanced mode allows seeing the actual accounts and journal entries.

Mobile UI for creating a Payment: if paying a supplier, the user could just go to that Purchase Invoice and tap "Pay Now", then enter amount and select cash or bank. The app then marks it paid and creates the ledger entry. For receiving from a customer, could do the same from Sales Invoice "Receive Payment".

**Reporting**: The P&L and Balance Sheet can be shown but with an option for simplified language. For example, P&L might be labeled "Income minus Expenses Report", showing just key headings: Total Income, Total Expense, Net Profit. The user can tap to expand categories if they want detail. Balance Sheet might be "What You Have and What You Owe", showing assets (cash, receivables, stock), liabilities (payables, loans), and net worth. These are static reports updated in real-time with transactions.

**Offline Capabilities:** Much of accounting happens automatically via other modules. If those modules function offline (e.g., an offline sale or a logged expense), then the underlying accounting entries will queue and sync. For example, a POS sale offline still creates a sales invoice and payment internally; that will sync to the server later and update accounts.
