The Accounting module interface itself (reports) might not be available offline in full because it needs up-to-date aggregate data. However, the app could cache the last known dashboard values or reports from last sync for reference. Logging a payment or expense offline is possible - say you pay a supplier in cash while offline, you can record that payment in the app; it will mark the invoice as paid locally and queue the payment entry. Upon syncing, the central records update. The system takes care to prevent duplicate payment entries (for instance, if two users try to log the same payment offline, which is unlikely in a small biz scenario with one bookkeeper, but possible with multiple staff).

In short, any transaction entry can be done offline (the forms are available), but consolidated views (like trial balance) may only refresh when online and synced.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Sizwe runs a general dealer. He isn't an accountant, but he uses TOSS to keep track of finances. Every sale and purchase already flows into TOSS Accounting without extra work - so at month's end, he checks the_ _Money In/Out_ _dashboard: it says "Income: R50,000, Expenses: R40,000, Left: R10,000 (Profit)" for that month. This makes sense to him immediately. He also notices 2_ _Unpaid Sales_ _where some customers bought on credit; the Accounting module lists them with names and amounts (almost like an_ _"Owed to You"_ _list). He can politely remind those customers. He also sees_ _Upcoming Bills_\* - his rent and an invoice from a supplier - so he ensures enough cash is reserved.

During the month, Sizwe had some cash expenses: buying diesel for the generator (not from a usual supplier). He taps "Record Expense", selects category "Utilities/Fuel", enters R200, and marks it as paid from Cash. TOSS adds that to his expenses. He also paid his one staff member their weekly wages - he records this as an expense under "Wages" category, R800. All this while offline (as the connectivity in the village is spotty), but the app saved it. Later, when he gets a signal, these entries sync and his accountant (who reviews things quarterly) will see them too.

When Sizwe's accountant logs in (maybe via a desktop web interface of TOSS), she can switch to an **Accountant View** that shows the full chart of accounts and ledger. She verifies that all sales and purchase entries have proper ledgers (they do). She uses the **Journal Entry** tool to record depreciation of Sizwe's refrigerator asset and to adjust for a small loan interest. These require her expertise, but Sizwe doesn't have to worry - he just sees the updated net profit. At year's end, the accountant prints out a formal Income Statement and Balance Sheet from TOSS for tax filing, while Sizwe continues to rely on the simple daily view that TOSS provides him to run the business.\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** In the Accounting module, the AI acts as a **financial advisor** watching over the books. A vital feature is **cash flow forecasting and alerts**[\[28\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L114-L117). The AI will project upcoming cash inflows (based on open invoices, regular sales) against outflows (upcoming supplier payments, recurring expenses like rent) to warn the owner of any cash crunch. For example, "Alert: You have R5,000 due to suppliers next week, but based on recent sales you might only have R3,000 - consider reducing expenses or finding funds"[\[28\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L114-L117). This early warning can be crucial for small businesses to avoid surprise shortfalls.

Another insight: **expense analysis**. The AI can analyze expenses and flag unusual spikes ("Your electricity expense this month is 30% higher than usual") or identify areas to save costs ("Your phone data expenses are high relative to sales - consider a different plan"). It might also benchmark against similar businesses in the network (anonymously): "Shops like yours spend on average 5% of revenue on transport, you are spending 10%" - prompting Sizwe to investigate why or collaborate on delivery costs.

For revenue, AI can highlight profitability: which product lines have the best margins and which barely break even. If integrated with the inventory data, it can compute an approximate **gross profit margin** per item and advise dropping or repricing items with consistently low or negative margins (maybe due to waste or pricing issues). For instance, "Eggs were often sold at a loss after accounting for breakage - consider adjusting price or supplier."

The AI also ensures **compliance reminders**: if tax is enabled, it might say "VAT return due in 10 days, expected payment RX" (calculating from records). Or for formal businesses, "Don't forget to pay staff UIF/PAYE by the 7th."

Additionally, AI can encourage good practices: if a business hasn't reconciled its bank in a while (for those that do), it nudges them. Or if the owner tends to withdraw too much cash (owner's drawings), it could caution about depleting business capital.

In summary, the AI in Accounting serves to make financial management proactive and intelligible - catching issues a human might miss and translating the numbers into plain advice.

**Collaborative Network Features:** While accounting data is usually private, the network layer allows certain cooperative financial activities:

- **Group Financial Benchmarking:** Participating businesses can opt to compare financial metrics anonymously. TOSS could provide a feature where an owner sees how they stack up: e.g., "Your profit margin this quarter is 20%, the network average for retail shops is 25%." This helps identify if one's doing well or needs improvement in areas like cost control or pricing. All data shared would be aggregated and anonymized (no individual numbers revealed).
- **Creditworthiness & Group Funding:** If businesses want to access loans or credit as a group, they may allow a combined financial statement to be generated. The Collaborative layer could aggregate selected financial info (like total sales, net incomes of each, etc.) to present to a microfinance institution or an NGO for funding consideration. For example, 10 spazas apply for a group loan - the lender gets a consolidated view of the group's finances through TOSS (with permission). TOSS could even facilitate **peer guarantees** - where businesses can pledge to back each other's loans, recorded through a network agreement.
- **Multi-Entity Accounting:** In some cases, a cooperative might have a central entity plus individual member accounts. TOSS's multi-tenant design keeps them separate by default, but network features could help with things like **inter-company ledgers**. For example, when two shops do a stock transfer sale, one's books show a sale and the other a purchase automatically (which TOSS can post via linked entries across tenants).
- **Shared Services Costs:** If the network collectively pays for something (say a shared delivery truck or marketing campaign), TOSS can allocate the expense to each member's Accounting. For instance, a R1000 bill for group advertising is split evenly among 5 businesses - the system can inject an expense of R200 in each of their books (perhaps through an automated journal entry) after consensus. This requires trust and setup that likely a network admin or group feature would manage.

Given privacy concerns, any financial collaboration is opt-in and highly transparent. Likely, these features will be used in formal cooperatives or trusted groups rather than random businesses on the platform. Still, the infrastructure being multi-tenant with events allows such flows.

An example: _A group of 5 mechanics share a costly machine. They agree that each will contribute monthly to its maintenance fund. TOSS could create an automated schedule that each tenant (mechanic's account) gets a monthly expense "Equipment Fund Contribution" and one central account (maybe the coop account) logs the incoming contributions. This ensures everyone's books reflect their share of the cost._

Such collaborative accounting ensures fairness and clarity in shared financial commitments, reinforcing trust in group endeavors.

## Manufacturing (Production Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Manufacturing module helps businesses plan and manage the process of converting raw materials into finished products. For ERP-III, it covers everything from defining the **Bill of Materials (BOM)** for a product, scheduling production, issuing raw materials, to tracking work in progress and completed goods[\[41\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=The%20Manufacturing%20module%20in%20ERPNext,conduct%20various%20manufacturing%20operations%20effectively). In a township context, this could apply to small-scale manufacturers like bakeries, clothing makers, furniture workshops, etc. The module ensures that these businesses can efficiently produce goods, control their production costs, and maintain quality, all integrated with inventory and purchasing.

**Core Workflows:** Key manufacturing workflows include:

- **Bill of Materials (BoM) Definition:** Create a **BoM** for each manufactured item, listing all raw materials (and quantities) and perhaps labor or machine operations needed to produce one unit[\[42\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,work%20orders%20based%20on%20MoMs). E.g., a BoM for one loaf of bread might include 500g flour, 300ml water, 10g yeast, etc. BOMs can be multi-level (if sub-assemblies exist), but many small businesses will have single-level BOMs.
- **Production Planning:** Optionally, plan production based on demand. The user (or AI) decides how many units to make in a batch. **Production Plan** functionality can take Sales Orders or stock replenishment targets as input and suggest production quantities and schedule[\[43\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,insights%20into%20production%20performance%2C%20costs). For instance, if a bakery has orders for 100 loaves and expects storefront sales of 50, they plan a batch of 150 loaves tomorrow.
- **Work Order (Job Order) Execution:** Create a **Work Order** (Manufacturing Order) to manufacture a certain quantity of a product[\[44\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,meet%20quality%20standards%20through%20inspections). This is the authorization to produce. It specifies the product, quantity, and target completion date. Once a work order is submitted, it may reserve raw materials (or at least check availability).
- **Material Issue & Production:** When starting production, **Issue Raw Materials** from stock to Work in Progress (WIP). This could be through a Stock Entry of type Manufacture: it moves the required components from stores to the WIP (or directly consumes them). Then, **Completion**: once production is done, **Receive Finished Goods** into stock (and record any unconsumed raw material returned or wastage).
- **Job Cards/Operations (if detailed):** For more complex processes, define **Workstations** (e.g., oven, sewing machine) and **Operations** (steps like mixing, baking) with durations and maybe assign workers. **Job Cards** can track progress of each operation on the shop floor[\[45\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,and%20optimizing%20production%20runs%20to). In a simple scenario, this might be overkill, but it's available if needed (e.g., a dressmaker might have cutting and stitching operations).
- **Quality Inspection:** If quality checks are needed for finished goods (or intermediate), integrate with Quality module - e.g., automatically create a Quality Inspection for a batch produced. If items fail QA, mark as rejected or rework.
- **Manufacturing Reports:** Track production efficiency - actual vs. planned material usage, yield, time taken. For instance, if always more flour is used than BOM suggests, maybe BOM needs updating or process needs improvement.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **BoM Consistency:** A BoM can't have circular references (product including itself). The system ensures that all raw items exist in the item master and that quantities make sense (no zero or negative usage). Also, a BoM can be marked as default for producing that item.
- **Material Availability Check:** Before starting a Work Order, the system can check if required raw materials are available in stock. If not, it should prompt to procure or produce those first (or allow starting partially if that's allowed). A rule could be: can't start work order unless at least X% of materials are available.
- **Backflush vs Manual Issue:** The module can operate in backflush mode (automatically deduct raw materials upon completion based on BOM) or manual issue mode. If backflush is used, completing a Work Order will consume the exact BoM quantities from inventory. If manual, the user must issue materials via a separate step. The system enforces whichever mode is configured and prevents double consumption.
- **Work Order Quantity Flexibility:** If actual output is different from planned (maybe scrap or extra yield), system allows closing a Work Order with a different finished quantity, but it should warn if significantly different. Also, any variance in raw material usage should be recordable (waste, etc.).
- **Status Progression:** Work Order statuses: Draft → In Process (when started) → Completed (when finished goods produced) → Closed. Only one completion allowed unless using partial completion (some systems allow producing in tranches). The rules ensure you can't complete more than ordered unless explicitly allowed (over-production).
- **Costing:** The manufacturing module calculates production cost (sum of raw materials + overhead/labor). If integrated to accounts, upon completion, it can optionally post a **Manufacturing Journal**: credit WIP and raw material stock, debit finished goods stock with total cost[\[46\]](https://www.sigzen.com/erpnext/production-management/#:~:text=Image%3A%20check). This keeps inventory values accurate. The system must ensure cost roll-up is done (especially if any raw materials had no value set, it alerts).
- **Time Tracking (if used):** If operations have time, and job cards track actual time, the system might compare planned vs actual time. Business rule: any operation exceeding time could flag delay or cost overrun. If labor costs are tracked, those get added to production cost.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **BOM (Bill of Materials):** Fields - Product (finished good item), Quantity (usually 1 unit BOM), list of BOM Items (raw materials and qty required for that quantity), and possibly Operations (if routing defined). Also fields like BOM cost (materials + operation cost).
- **Work Order (Production Order):** Fields - Product to manufacture, Quantity to produce, BOM reference, Planned start date, Planned end date, actual start/end, status, and links to stock movements. It might have a child table for operations status if applicable.
- **Job Card (if used):** Fields - Operation, Work Order, workstation, assigned to (person), start time, end time, status (not started/started/completed), actual time taken.
- **Operation:** Fields - Operation name, description, workstation type or default, standard time per unit or batch.
- **Workstation:** Fields - Name of machine or station, capacity info (like hours available), maybe cost rate.
- **Stock Entries for Manufacture:** Same Stock Entry doctype but with type = Manufacture. It will have two sets of child items: consumed materials and produced goods. Key fields - Work Order reference, and for each consumed item (source warehouse), for produced item (target warehouse).
- **Material Request (Manufacturing type):** Optionally, if a production plan suggests to manufacture something, it may raise a request to produce.

**User Interface & Experience:** For small-scale manufacturing, the UI should simplify the process - possibly through a guided wizard or checklists:

For example, a **Work Order screen** might show: 1. Required materials and their availability (with a "Pick Materials" button to issue them). 2. A "Start Production" button to indicate production is underway (which could start a timer if tracking time, or just mark status). 3. A "Finish Production" button to record output quantity, scrap, etc., and automatically receive finished stock.

If using operations: once "Start" is hit, it could spawn tasks for each operation (job cards) which a user can mark as done. However, in many cases, that might be overkill - so the default UI might skip that unless turned on.

The BOM editor UI would allow adding materials easily, perhaps even with a recipe-like feel ("Add Ingredient" lines). On mobile, listing ingredients and quantities can be a simple form. Possibly allow capturing by scanning items to add them to BOM.

The **Manufacturing dashboard** might show open work orders and their progress, and maybe a calendar of planned production. If a user is producing daily, a simple list "Today's Production: item X - 100 units planned" could be shown.

Integration with inventory is key in UI: a user in the Work Order can tap "Check Stock & Reserve" which will show which raw materials are short, and perhaps a quick action to create a Purchase Order for those if needed.

Mobile usage scenario: A small bakery owner uses her phone to initiate a bread baking work order in the morning. The UI might have a special shortcut: "Make Product" where she selects "Bread" and enters 100 loaves. The system then does everything behind scenes: checks ingredients, suggests issuing them. She confirms she has enough flour, etc. She hits "Start". After baking, she hits "Finish - 100 made, 2 spoiled" maybe, and the system updates stock of bread and reduces stock of flour, yeast accordingly. This condenses multiple steps into a user-friendly sequence.

**Offline Capabilities:** Manufacturing operations often happen on-site where the server might not be reachable (imagine a workshop with thick walls or a remote area with poor connectivity). So TOSS allows production transactions offline as well. If a user starts a Work Order offline, it will be saved locally. They can issue materials (the app will still need to know current raw material stock, so it uses last synced data as reference - possibly warns if uncertain). They then mark completion offline. All these will sync and adjust central inventory when back online. To avoid major mismatches, maybe heavy manufacturing might mostly be done with some connectivity to update stock immediately (especially if raw materials are also being used in sales etc.), but the system will handle any double-use gracefully via sync conflict resolution (e.g., if offline work order consumed some flour while at the same time a POS sale sold flour, when syncing one may drive stock negative or cause an alert requiring reconciliation).

For recording job times offline (if job cards on a machine without internet), the app caching allows stamping start/stop times and then syncing them.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Neo runs a small dairy, producing cheese from milk collected from local farmers. Each week, he uses TOSS Manufacturing to plan production. He has a BOM for "Fresh Cheese (1kg)" which includes 10 liters of milk, culture, rennet, and salt. On Monday, Neo creates a_ _Work Order_ _for 50kg of Fresh Cheese to fulfill expected demand. TOSS shows he needs 500 liters of milk and other ingredients. He checks the stock: TOSS shows he has enough culture and salt, but only 300 liters of milk on hand. Via the app, he quickly generates a_ _Material Request_\* to procure the extra 200 liters from farmers (which Purchasing module will handle). By Tuesday, milk arrives and he records the Purchase Receipt for it, updating stock.

Now Neo issues the materials to production: he uses the "Pick Materials" function on the Work Order, which deducts 500 liters of milk and the required amounts of other ingredients from inventory into WIP. He starts production (he doesn't use detailed operations; he just needs to track start and end). After a day of work, he ends with 48kg of cheese (lost some yield in process). In TOSS, he completes the Work Order, entering actual output 48kg. The system consumes the materials (if any left unused, he could adjust, but in this case, all 500L used) and increases stock of Fresh Cheese by 48 units of 1kg each. The system also records the production cost: it knows how much he paid for the milk (and an overhead rate he set for labor), so it calculates cost per kg. Neo can now see that cost vs. his selling price to ensure profit.

During this, TOSS's Quality module popped up a reminder for **Quality Check**: one in five batches should be tested for moisture content. He performs a quick test and logs the result in a Quality Inspection linked to the Work Order, all within the app.

All of Neo's manufacturing entries were done in a remote dairy with spotty internet, so they queued up and synced in the evening when he got better signal. The stock levels for cheese and milk then updated on the central server, and an **Accounting** entry was posted moving the value of ingredients to the value of produced cheese.

Neo also uses the Manufacturing module for maintenance of equipment indirectly; every 100 batches, the machine needs service - TOSS tracks how many Work Orders have been done and alerts him at the right interval (via Maintenance in Support module).\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The AI in manufacturing serves as a production planner and process optimizer. It can do **demand forecasting**: analyzing sales trends to suggest production quantities. For example, "Based on the last 4 weeks of sales, you should produce 10% more Mageu drink this week to meet rising demand[\[30\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L274-L282)." Conversely, if sales are dropping, it warns not to over-produce to avoid wastage. The AI also looks at **production efficiency**: it knows the expected yield from BOM vs actual recorded output. If consistently the actual output is lower, it will highlight this: "Your yield for beef biltong is averaging 90% of expected - check for process losses or update the BOM to reflect reality." If actual usage of raw mats is higher than BOM, it suggests checking for waste or theft.

Another AI feature is **Material Requirements Planning (MRP)** automation[\[47\]](https://www.sigzen.com/erpnext/production-management/#:~:text=). Instead of the user manually planning, the AI can automatically generate production plans. For instance, it sees low stock of a manufactured item and pending demand, so it could auto-create a draft Work Order (or at least recommend: "You should make 200 more units of Soap this month, will require X of ingredients - create Work Order?"). It also coordinates with purchasing: if a planned production will require more raw materials than available, the AI triggers a purchase suggestion (or auto-draft PO) for those raw mats, aligning procurement with production.

For scheduling, if multiple products use the same equipment, the AI can help avoid clashes and suggest an optimal sequence (especially if one product's output can be input for another or to minimize cleanup time between products, etc.). In a simple example, if a bakery makes both bread and cakes and has one oven, the AI might schedule bread first then cakes based on oven time needed and due times.

Quality-wise, AI can correlate quality results with process parameters, if data is available, to warn if certain trends might cause quality issues (this might be advanced, though - likely later).

**Collaborative Network Features:** In manufacturing, network collaboration might involve **outsourcing or subcontracting** between businesses. For example, one community bakery might have an oven capacity to also bake goods for smaller bakers. TOSS could allow a Work Order to be assigned to another business in the network (subcontracting)[\[48\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L430-L438). The system would then facilitate the inter-company transaction: one business provides raw materials to the other (or the other uses its own and charges), and finished goods are returned. The Collaborative layer would share the production request and track it. This way, smaller players can utilize idle capacity in the network.

Another scenario is **shared production planning** for complementary products. Suppose a co-op of seamstresses each makes different clothing items but share a pool of fabric bulk-bought. They could use TOSS to coordinate production schedules so that the fabric rolls are allocated fairly and orders are met collectively on time. This is more of a human coordination aided by transparency: each sees the overall production calendar (if permitted) and resource availability.

The network can also collectively negotiate raw material purchases for manufacturing (ties into group buying from Buying module), ensuring manufacturers get bulk rates on inputs like flour, fabric, etc., which lowers cost of production for all. TOSS would integrate that by linking production plans to those group purchases.

There's also knowledge sharing: proven BOMs or processes could be templatized and shared via the platform. E.g., one cheesemaker shares their BOM and process (maybe not exact secret recipe proportions if they don't want, but some may share best practices) - new entrepreneurs can import a BOM template from a public library as a starting point. This isn't exactly a network transaction, more of a communal knowledge base.

From a data perspective, the network could aggregate production metrics: total goods produced in the network, capacity usage, etc., useful if presenting to potential investors or development programs ("Our network of 5 bakeries produces 1000 loaves/day feeding X community").

In summary, manufacturing collaboration in TOSS allows distributed production resources to be used more efficiently, fosters subcontracting (which can create intra-network supply chains), and helps small manufacturers band together for economies of scale in input buying and process improvement.

## Projects (Project Management Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Projects module helps businesses plan and track project-based work - any initiative with multiple tasks, a timeline, and possibly resource assignments. This could range from client projects (like a construction job, event management, consulting task) to internal projects (like shop renovations or marketing campaigns). The module provides tools to break work into **tasks**, assign responsibilities, log time or progress, and ensure projects are delivered on schedule and within budget. It gives a structured approach to what might otherwise be managed in notebooks or not at all. For small organizations, this means even a one-off project (e.g., catering a big event, fulfilling a large order) can be managed systematically, increasing the chance of success and customer satisfaction[\[49\]](https://discuss.frappe.io/c/erpnext/projects/53#:~:text=Welcome%20to%20the%20ERPNext%20Proejcts,discuss%2C%20and%20help%20other%20communi%E2%80%A6).

**Core Workflows:** Key features and flows in Projects include:

- **Project Creation:** Create a **Project** entry for each distinct project or job. Define basic info: name, start and end date, client (if applicable), budget or expected revenue, and project type (internal vs external).
- **Task Breakdown:** Under each project, define **Tasks** that need to be completed[\[49\]](https://discuss.frappe.io/c/erpnext/projects/53#:~:text=Welcome%20to%20the%20ERPNext%20Proejcts,discuss%2C%20and%20help%20other%20communi%E2%80%A6). Each task has a description, an assignee (who will do it), a due date, and perhaps a status (Not Started, In Progress, Completed). Tasks may have dependencies (Task B can only start after Task A finishes, etc.) which can be noted.
- **Assignments & Team:** Assign tasks to team members or responsible persons. In small biz context, the "team" might be just the owner and one helper, but it could also involve external collaborators. Each assignee should be able to view their tasks easily (maybe via ToDo integration).
- **Time Tracking & Work Logs:** If needed, users can log **time (timesheets)** against tasks[\[50\]](https://discuss.frappe.io/t/about-the-project-management-category/56267#:~:text=About%20the%20Project%20Management%20category,category%2C%20you%20can%20post). For example, an electrician logs 5 hours spent on wiring (under a project for a shop installation). This is useful for projects billed on time & material or for measuring productivity. Timesheets can be consolidated to see total effort.
- **Progress Tracking:** Update task status or percent complete as work progresses. The project has an overall completion percentage based on tasks done. If using milestones, the project might have key milestones to mark.
- **Project Cost/Revenues:** Optionally link project to financials. Sales Invoices or Expenses can be tagged to a project so that one can compute profitability per project. E.g., a construction project might accumulate material costs (from Purchase Invoices) and revenue from a client invoice, all tied to that project.
- **Project Closure & Evaluation:** Once all tasks are done, mark project Completed/Closed. Possibly capture a summary or lessons learned.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Task Date Consistency:** The system ensures that task dates fall within the project's overall dates. If a task is set to end after project's end date, it could warn or auto-adjust project end.
- **Mandatory Fields:** Tasks should have either an assignee or a clear owner, and a due date for proper tracking. The system might nag if tasks are created without due dates.
- **Dependency Enforcement:** If Task B depends on Task A, the system could optionally prevent marking B as started until A is completed, or at least warn. And if A is delayed, possibly flag that B will slip.
- **Project Status Auto-Update:** When all tasks are marked complete, the system can auto-mark the project as Completed. Conversely, if any task reopens, project reopens.
- **Budget vs Actual:** If a project budget (cost or time) is set, the system tracks actual expenses or hours logged. If actuals exceed budget, it flags it. E.g., "Project X is over budget by 10%" or "Task Y took 15h vs planned 10h."
- **Permission Control:** Possibly restrict who can view certain projects if sensitive. For instance, only team members can see project details. (In small teams likely open, but the system supports that for bigger setups.)
- **Client Access:** Not likely in MVP, but ERPNext allows a client to have portal view of their project. That could be considered: a customer might log in to see progress of a project they commissioned (like a house renovation progress, with photos in tasks). But enabling that requires careful scoping.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Project:** Fields - Project Name, Customer (if any), Status, % Complete (calculated), Start Date, End Date, Project Manager (owner of project), Budgeted Cost/Hours, and possibly a description or scope statement.
- **Task:** Fields - Task Name, Description, Project (link), Assigned To, Status, Start and Due Date, Priority, Depends On (link to another task), and maybe field for actual hours spent vs estimated hours.
- **Timesheet/Work Log:** (If using ERPNext's Timesheets, or a simplified internal log) - Fields: Task, User, Date, Hours, Work Done description. Timesheets might roll up into payroll or billing if needed.
- **Project Update/Issue:** Some systems track issues or updates separate from tasks. Possibly not needed; tasks and comments can cover it. But could have a child doctype like "Project Milestone" or "Risk/Issue" log if advanced.
- **Link to Docs:** Many documents can have a "Project" field (Sales Order, Invoice, Purchase Order, Delivery, Expense, Timesheet). That association allows filtering by project in accounts and stock movements. So the data model extends beyond just project module tables - it's integrated through links.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Projects module UI provides both list and timeline views. For each project, a **Gantt chart** view is valuable to visualize tasks against dates. In a simple mobile scenario, maybe a list sorted by due date with indentations for dependencies suffices, but a small Gantt or timeline could be shown (the Creative Tim design or similar might have such component to leverage).

There could also be a **Kanban view** for tasks by status (To Do, Doing, Done) for users who prefer that style of tracking tasks.

The Project dashboard shows key info: number of open tasks, tasks due this week, any overdue tasks. It might also show budget vs actual if financial tracking is on (e.g., "Spent R8,000 of R10,000 budget").

Task management on mobile: likely through a unified "My Tasks" view across projects. A user opens the app and sees tasks assigned to them, due dates, and can check them off or update. They can also add quick tasks if something new comes up, and assign to themselves or others.

For project managers (could be the owner or a team lead), they can adjust tasks, reassign, and comment. The ability to add comments or attachments to tasks helps share updates or photos of progress (like a completed milestone picture).

**Offline Capabilities:** Managing tasks and projects offline is feasible in terms of data (lists of tasks can be cached; new tasks or updates can queue). If someone is at a worksite with no internet, they can update task statuses or log hours, and those sync later. The main challenge offline might be the Gantt or heavy visuals - but the app can degrade gracefully to lists when offline.

All task data entered offline (e.g., marking a task complete, or adding a new task that was noticed as needed) will sync and update the project once online. If two team members offline make conflicting changes (rare in small teams), last sync might win and require manual merge (like if both change a task status differently).

Attachments (like photos) taken offline can also queue for upload when online, which is useful for evidence of work done.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Thandi runs a small construction firm that builds rural classrooms. She uses TOSS Projects to manage each building project. For a new classroom build, she creates a_ _Project_ _"Lotus Primary Classroom Block" and enters the start date (March 1) and expected completion (May 30). She lists out_ _Tasks_\*: Foundation, Walls, Roofing, Finishing, etc., each with due dates and assigns them to her foreman or subcontractors. The system displays a timeline of these tasks. As work begins, the foreman marks the "Foundation" task as started and then completed a week later, noting in comments that extra cement was needed due to soil conditions. TOSS captures the actual finish date, and Thandi sees on the Gantt that subsequent tasks (Walls) can start.

During the build, Thandi buys materials which she tags under this project in the Buying module. She also logs labor hours via timesheets (her workers' hours are recorded against tasks in the project). The project dashboard shows that 60% of tasks are done and also aggregates costs: materials + labor so far, comparing to her budget.

One task "Roofing" is dependent on "Walls" completion. If Walls get delayed, TOSS flags Roofing as at-risk of delay too. Thandi receives a notification: "Project Lotus Primary - Roofing task might miss its start date due to delay in Walls." She can then act (maybe add more workers to catch up).

By project end, Thandi has a clear record of all activities. She closes the project. Later, when bidding for another job, she can look back at this project's data to estimate time and cost (learning that foundation took extra time due to local soil - knowledge to incorporate). If needed, she could even share a summary with the school committee: e.g., timeline and expenses, demonstrating transparency and good management.\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The AI in Projects functions like a project management assistant. It can do **timeline predictions**: based on progress and past projects, it might foresee that a project will not meet the deadline and warn proactively[\[51\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L360-L364). For example, "Task 'Walls' is 5 days behind schedule, the overall project completion is trending 1 week late." The AI could then suggest corrective actions like reallocating resources or extending work hours.

AI can also help with **effort estimation**. If a user is creating a new project similar to a past one, the system can suggest task durations or resource needs based on historical data ("Last time a similar event planning took 40 hours of work; plan for something similar"). This is especially helpful for small business owners who might not have formal project estimation skills.

For active projects, the AI monitors any **deviations**: budget overruns, scope creep (tasks being added frequently), or idle time (tasks not started days after planned start). It will nudge the project owner with simple advice: "Project X has tasks that should have started but haven't - do you need to reschedule?" or "You're 75% through time but only 50% tasks done."

Another AI aspect is **resource leveling**: if one person is assigned 10 tasks all due this week and another has few, AI can spot the overload and suggest redistributing tasks if possible.

For billing projects, AI can ensure no billable work is missed - e.g., if timesheets are logged, it can remind, "You have 10 unbilled hours for Project Y, create an invoice?" (This touches Sales module to generate an invoice for services, but AI coordinates the prompt.)

**Collaborative Network Features:** Projects might be shared across businesses for joint initiatives. For example, multiple contractors could collaborate on a single large project (like building a community center: one does plumbing, another electrical, etc.). TOSS could allow a project to have tasks assigned to different tenant users in the network (with appropriate sharing). Each business sees only the tasks relevant to them (plus maybe overall timeline if needed), and they can update progress. The central project owner (perhaps the main contractor) sees the whole picture. This fosters **multi-company project collaboration** with clear responsibility demarcation.

There's also potential for **community projects or events** planning via TOSS: say a group of local businesses plan a joint fair. They set up a project in TOSS, share it among them, assign each other tasks (one handles venue, another marketing, etc.). Everyone can view progress. It's like a shared to-do list for the event, ensuring accountability.

Additionally, network might offer **expertise sharing**: if a business is new to project management, they could use templates from others. A more experienced user could publish a project template (like "Standard Home Renovation Project Plan") with tasks and timelines, which others can copy and adapt. This raises overall project management maturity in the network.

Permission and data control: cross-tenant tasks would likely just show minimal needed info to the collaborator. If they log time or expenses, those would reflect in their own books but also update the main project metrics through event linking (maybe by summarizing completion percentage or sending cost info if needed under an agreed contract).

For example, _the community center build involves 3 companies. Each has their own TOSS tenant. The main contractor creates Project "Community Center" and invites the plumber and electrician companies to join via the network. In TOSS, behind the scenes, it creates a project stub in each of their systems or at least tasks assigned to them that appear in their task list. They update progress on plumbing and electrical tasks respectively. The main contractor's view aggregates this (plumbing 100% done, electrical 50% done). If the main contractor linked a milestone payment to electrical completion, TOSS could notify when that task hits 100%._

This way, projects spanning multiple parties can be coordinated without everyone being in the same company record, respecting the multi-tenant separation but bridging via the collaborative layer.

## HR (Human Resources & Payroll Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The HR module manages **employee information and basic HR processes** such as attendance, leave (time off), payroll, and perhaps recruitment. For small businesses, this module keeps track of the people working in the business - be it a handful of employees or part-time helpers - and automates calculations like salaries or wages, leave balances, etc. It ensures that even without a dedicated HR person, things like paying employees on time and keeping records of their leave and performance are handled systematically[\[52\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=What%20features%20are%20available%20in,the%20HR%20module%20of%20ERPNext).

**Core Workflows:**

- **Employee Records:** Create an **Employee** profile for each staff member (or even the owner for payroll purposes). This includes personal details, contact info, role/title, date of joining, salary details, etc. For a small biz, maybe just name, phone, job title, and pay rate are the main fields.
- **Attendance Tracking:** Optionally, mark daily **Attendance** for employees[\[53\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=The%20HR%20module%20in%20ERPNext,service). This could be manual (the owner ticks off who came in each day) or via an integration (biometric or simply the employee logging check-in via app if trust). For casual businesses, this might be skipped, but for those with hourly wages, it's important.
- **Leave (Vacation/Sick Days):** Manage **Leave Application** workflow[\[54\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=How%20does%20ERPNext%20track%20employee,attendance). Employees (or owner on their behalf) apply for leave specifying type (Annual leave, Sick leave, etc.) and dates. The system keeps a tally of how many days taken and remaining (if they have an allowance).
- **Payroll Processing:** Based on employee salary info, generate **Payslips** or a Payroll Entry each pay period[\[55\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=Can%20ERPNext%20handle%20payroll%20processing%3F). For example, monthly payroll: system pulls each employee's salary, adds any earnings (overtime, commissions) and deductions (loan repayment, absence without leave, etc.), calculates taxes or contributions if needed, and produces a payslip. The owner can review and finalize, then record the salary payment.
- **Expense Claims & Reimbursements:** If employees spend their own money on business expenses, they can file an **Expense Claim** (with receipts attached). The system then logs it and can add reimbursement to payroll or prompt a separate payment.
- **Recruitment (if needed):** Possibly manage **Job Openings** and **Applicants** if the business is hiring, although this might be overkill for MVP. But a simple applicant tracker can be included (ERPNext has it).
- **Performance (future maybe):** For now likely not, but could have simple **Appraisals** or at least notes on performance in the employee record.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Unique Employee ID:** Each employee should have a unique identifier (employee number). The system could generate or allow using, say, national ID as key if needed.
- **Attendance vs Leave Reconciliation:** If someone is on approved leave, system might auto-mark them as on leave on attendance record to avoid confusion. Or disallow marking present when on leave.
- **Leave Balance Check:** When approving a leave application, the system ensures the employee has enough leave days left of that type. If not, it may allow but flag as unpaid leave or require override.
- **Payroll Calculations Accuracy:** All components in payroll (like if tax calculation is needed) must follow defined formula. For example, for South Africa, it would incorporate PAYE tax tables, UIF, etc., if the user opts in. But for simplicity, initial payroll might just be gross pay and net pay if they don't handle taxes (most small micro enterprises might not unless formal).
- **Payslip Approval:** Possibly require a review step, or at least once payroll is processed, mark it as final. Prevent changes to past payroll unless via proper adjustments (for audit trail).
- **Confidentiality:** Salary info should be restricted to authorized roles (owner, maybe accountant). TOSS should ensure that normal employees using the app cannot see other's salaries or HR data (row-level permission by employee).
- **Statutory Compliance:** If configured, ensure calculations like provident fund or tax are in line with rules. Could also include auto-generation of payslip slips or statutory reports (like UIF declarations if needed).
- **Contract End Alerts:** If an employee is on contract with an end date, system can alert HR a month before expiry to decide renewal or termination.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Employee:** Fields - Name, Employee ID, Date of Joining, Department/Designation (if any), Salary info (could be structured as components: basic, allowances, etc., or simply a rate), Pay Frequency (monthly, weekly), Leave allocation (like 15 annual leave days/year), Status (Active/Left), maybe Bank account for salary transfer.
- **Attendance:** Fields - Employee, Date, Status (Present, Absent, Half Day, etc.), maybe check-in/out times if needed.
- **Leave Type:** Master specifying types (Annual Paid Leave, Sick Leave, etc.) and rules (like whether it accrues, whether encashable).
- **Leave Allocation:** For each employee, how many days of each leave type they get (yearly or total). Alternatively, could compute based on joining date and policy.
- **Leave Application:** Fields - Employee, Leave Type, From date, To date, Reason, Status (Applied, Approved, Rejected).
- **Salary Structure/Payslip:** ERPNext has Salary Structure (template of earning/deduction components) and Payslip which is actual for the period. Simplified approach: a payslip per employee per pay period listing Gross, Deductions, Net. Fields - Employee, Period (month), components (like Base Salary, Overtime, Tax, etc.), Net Pay, and whether paid.
- **Payroll Entry:** A batch entity representing a payroll run for a period. It can have all payslips under it for approval.
- **Expense Claim:** Fields - Employee, date, details of expenses (child table of expense items with amount, description), total, approved/rejected, and whether reimbursed (could link to a Payment entry or payslip).
- **Company (HR Settings):** Could hold general settings like standard work hours, holiday list (public holidays), etc.

**User Interface & Experience:** The HR module UI, for a small business, should be straightforward:

- **Employee Directory:** a simple list of employees with maybe photo, name, position, contact. Adding an employee is via a form with personal and job details.
- **Attendance marking:** Possibly a daily view where the owner can tick checkboxes for who's present. Or employees can mark themselves via the app if allowed (with maybe a PIN or something to avoid buddy punching).
- **Leave:** A screen showing each employee's leave balances and a quick way to apply for leave. If an employee uses the app, they can fill a leave form which sends to owner for approval (owner gets a notification and just taps approve or reject). The leave calendar can show upcoming time off so the owner knows who's out when.
- **Payroll:** A wizard or step-by-step for payroll each month. Step 1: pick month and employees (likely all active by default). Step 2: system generates draft payslips with base salary and any automatic deductions. Step 3: owner can edit any variable parts (e.g., add overtime hours or a bonus). Step 4: finalize and mark as paid. After finalizing, payslips can be viewed (and possibly printed or shared individually with employees).
- The UI for a payslip should show the breakdown: "Base Pay: R X, Overtime: R Y, Total Earnings: R Z. Deductions: Tax: R A, Other: R B, Total Deductions: R C. **Net Pay: R (Z-C)**."
- **Notifications:** The module will produce notifications like "Alice has applied for 2 days leave (Mar 5-6) for 'Medical'. Approve?" where the owner can click Approve right from notification if possible.
- **Self-Service:** If employees have limited access, they might be allowed to see their own payslips, apply for leave, and check their remaining leave days via the app (but not see others').
- Possibly a **Team Calendar** combining both schedule tasks (if Projects to person) and leave, so the owner sees who is available.

**Offline Capabilities:** HR functions like attendance and leave can be recorded offline if needed. For example, if the store is offline in the morning, the owner can still tick attendance; it will sync later with date/time stamps. Employees applying for leave offline can fill the form which queues up. The risk is if two offline devices both mark attendance for the same person differently (like one says present, one says absent), but typically one person (owner/manager) would handle attendance to avoid conflict.

Payslip generation likely would be done while online since it might need up-to-date tax rules or ensure all data is current, but in principle, a draft could be generated offline using cached data and sync calculations later. Payment disbursement might be recorded offline too (like note that salaries were paid in cash on a date, then sync).

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** \*Amina owns a tailoring shop with 3 employees. She uses TOSS HR to keep things organized. In the Employee section, she has profiles for her tailors with their start dates and salaries. Each morning, when the team arrives, Amina opens the Attendance page on her phone and marks everyone present (if someone is out sick, she marks Absent and the system will treat it accordingly). Last month, one employee, Sam, joined mid-month. TOSS automatically pro-rated his first salary.

One of her employees, Lerato, wants two days off next week for a family event. Lerato opens her TOSS app (with employee login) and submits a **Leave Application** for those days under "Annual Leave". Amina immediately gets an alert in her app: "Lerato requests Annual Leave from Sep 10 to Sep 11." Amina checks the schedule and approves it with one tap. TOSS deducts 2 days from Lerato's leave balance and marks those dates so Amina knows she'll be short-staffed then.

At the end of the month, Amina runs **Payroll**. She starts a Payroll Entry for the month. TOSS pulls each employee's salary: e.g., Lerato R3000, Sam R2500, Thabo R3000. Lerato took 2 leave days but she had enough leave balance, so it's paid leave (her salary remains full). Sam had one unpaid absence (was sick but no leave balance as he's new), so the system deducted one day's pay (R125) from his salary automatically. Amina reviews these on each draft payslip. Everything looks fine; she confirms and finalizes payroll. The app then marks those payslips as final. She records that she paid them in cash - each employee will sign a receipt outside the system. In TOSS, she just marks each payslip as Paid (maybe via a Bulk "Mark Paid").

Each employee can now see their **Payslip** on their phone - a simple breakdown so they understand how their pay was calculated (Sam sees one day deduction, which matches what Amina told him). This builds trust as everything is transparent and accurate[\[55\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=Can%20ERPNext%20handle%20payroll%20processing%3F).

Next, Amina also uses HR to track a loan she gave Thabo. She put it as a recurring deduction of R100 each month on his profile. The payslip reflected that deduction. After a few months, once fully deducted, she'll remove that deduction entry.

Finally, Amina's shop occasionally brings interns on stipends. She uses the employee records to note contract end dates. The system will remind her when an intern's contract is close to ending so she can decide on extension or prepare a parting certificate.\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The AI in HR can act like an HR advisor. For example, it monitors attendance patterns and might alert Amina: "Notice: Thabo has been late 3 times this week" or "Lerato has used 80% of her annual leave already, plan accordingly." It can also watch labor cost vs sales - "Your labor cost was 20% of sales this month, up from 15% last month[\[56\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L26-L34)." Such insight helps to ensure staffing levels are right. If integrated with scheduling (maybe via Projects or tasks), it could suggest optimizing shifts ("Fridays are busiest, ensure all staff are present or consider extra help").

For performance, if Amina does any ratings or the system infers from project task completions, AI could identify top performers or training needs ("Sam consistently finishes tasks 20% faster than estimated" or "Thabo seems to struggle with complex alterations - consider training").

For compliance, AI can remind of statutory things: "Remember to submit UIF form by 7th" (if relevant to those on payroll) or "It's time to review salaries, inflation was X% this year" as a gentle nudge for raises.

**Collaborative Network Features:** HR data is usually private, but some collaborative ideas: - **Shared Talent Pool:** Within a network, businesses could share a pool of pre-vetted temporary workers. TOSS could allow an employee (especially contractors or temp staff) to be "shared" across tenants. For instance, a driver might do deliveries for multiple shops. If the network has a feature for gig workers, a driver could have a profile visible to nearby businesses and they can log hours for him. Each business might pay him separately, but his single profile accumulates his experience. - **Group Benefits:** A network could negotiate group health insurance or similar for members' employees. TOSS could assist by providing aggregated employee counts, ages, etc., without personal details, to insurance providers, then help manage contributions if one is set up (like a deduction in payroll for insurance premium for those employees who opt in). - **Training events:** If a skill workshop is organized for the network's employees (say a customer service training), it can be managed as a project and HR link by marking which employees from which companies attended. So cross-tenant events and tracking can be done. - **Compliance help:** Possibly the network might collectively ensure labor law compliance (like everyone paying at least minimum wage, etc.). TOSS could alert if any salary is below known minimum wage law (if data is input). That might be more a core feature than network, but a network could share best practices and TOSS enforces them if the group decides (like all cooperative members must give 12 days leave - configured in system for all).

Primarily though, HR is internal. The collaborative aspects might come in for sharing resources (like a traveling expert that works short stints at different places, handled via timesheets across tenants) and collective welfare (using data to help all employees get something like easier access to loans - e.g., a microfinance might look at aggregated employment data via TOSS to lend to employees).

For example, _if an employee of one shop applies for a personal loan with a bank that's partnering with the TOSS network, with the employee's consent, TOSS could share their employment and income verification digitally (like how large companies provide employment letters). The network's credibility could make banks more comfortable lending to these individuals._ This isn't exactly HR collaboration between businesses, but leveraging the network for employee benefit.

## Support (Customer Support & Service Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Support module (Helpdesk) is designed to handle **customer issues, complaints, or service requests**. It ensures that when customers of the business have problems - say a product defect, a question, or a need for service - those issues are logged, tracked, and resolved efficiently[\[57\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,manage%20tickets%20by%20connecting%20your). For small businesses, this could be as simple as noting down customer complaints and making sure each is addressed (e.g., exchanging a damaged product, scheduling a service call, or answering an inquiry). It also covers **maintenance** and **warranty** management for businesses dealing with equipment (either their own or customer-owned assets that need servicing)[\[58\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/maintenance#:~:text=The%20maintenance%20schedule%20and%20maintenance,optimized%20ERP%20environment%20for%20users). The aim is to not let customer requests fall through the cracks and to maintain a good reputation through responsive support.

**Core Workflows:**

- **Issue/Ticket Logging:** When a customer contacts the business with a problem or request, create a **Support Issue (Ticket)** in TOSS[\[57\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,manage%20tickets%20by%20connecting%20your). Fields capture the customer, date, and description of the issue. Issues could come via email (if integrated), via the website (a form), or manually by staff entering details from a phone call or walk-in.
- **Issue Assignment & Prioritization:** Categorize the issue (e.g., Inquiry, Complaint, Technical Fault) and set a priority (Low/Medium/High/Urgent). Assign it to a team member or the person responsible for resolving it[\[59\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,how%20happy%20the%20customers%20are). For example, a technician might be assigned to fix an appliance under warranty.
- **Response & Resolution:** Communicate with the customer as needed - the module logs these communications (could integrate with email or WhatsApp). Staff add **Status updates** to the ticket: e.g., "In Progress - part ordered," then "Resolved - part replaced." All interactions (emails sent, calls made notes) can be recorded on the ticket timeline[\[57\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,manage%20tickets%20by%20connecting%20your).
- **SLA Management:** If Service Level Agreements (promised response times) are defined, the system monitors them[\[60\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,that%20have%20already%20been%20set). For instance, "respond to all complaints within 24h". The system will flag or escalate if an issue hasn't been responded to or resolved in the agreed time.
- **Closure & Feedback:** Once the issue is resolved to the customer's satisfaction, close the ticket. Optionally, capture customer feedback or a satisfaction level.
- **Maintenance Schedules:** For businesses that maintain equipment (like a shop might maintain its freezer or a co-op might share a generator), schedule **Maintenance Visits** using this module[\[58\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/maintenance#:~:text=The%20maintenance%20schedule%20and%20maintenance,optimized%20ERP%20environment%20for%20users). E.g., quarterly service of a machine - create a maintenance schedule and TOSS will spawn issues or tasks when service is due.
- **Warranty Claims:** If a sold product is under warranty and fails, log it as an issue with tag "Warranty." The system can track if it gets repaired, replaced, or if a claim must be sent to the supplier.
- **Knowledge Base:** Over time, collect common solutions in a **Knowledge Base** so that similar issues can be solved faster[\[61\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,tickets%20by%20connecting%20your%20email). E.g., an FAQ or troubleshooting guide accessible to staff (or even customers via website).

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Unique Ticket ID:** Each issue gets an ID for tracking (for example, SUP-0001). This ID can be shared with customer so they can refer to it.
- **Mandatory Details:** At least a contact (customer or name/phone) and issue description should be required to log a ticket, so nothing is too vague or orphaned.
- **SLA Timer:** If using SLAs, the system automatically sets deadlines (like must respond by X, resolve by Y based on priority) and escalates if not met. Escalation might mean notifying a manager or raising priority.
- **Ticket Status Flow:** Typically New → Open (assigned) → Work in Progress → Resolved/Pending Confirmation → Closed. The system might restrict certain transitions (e.g., can't close without marking resolved). If a customer says it's not solved, perhaps reopen.
- **Customer Portal Access:** If enabled, a customer could view their tickets on a portal and even open new ones. The system would validate their identity. But probably for MVP, support staff handle all entries.
- **Integration with Sales/Stock:** If a support issue results in a replacement product being issued, ideally that should link to a Delivery (stock out) or Sales Return. Business rule: any free replacement item should be recorded in inventory and perhaps tied to the original sale invoice (for warranty validation). Not enforced by support module itself, but procedure to ensure consistency.
- **Knowledge Base Updates:** Some places enforce that if an issue is of a certain type and resolved, a knowledge base entry is created or updated. We might not enforce, but encourage with UI prompts like "Document this solution in Knowledge Base?".

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Issue/Ticket:** Fields - Issue ID, Subject, Description, Customer (or just a contact name/phone for walk-ins not in system), Issue Type/Category, Priority, Status, Opening Date, Response Due Date (if SLA), Resolve Due Date, Assigned To, Resolution Summary, and links (like to an Item or Sales Invoice if relevant).
- **Issue Comment/Communication:** Possibly using the system's communication log or comments to record messages related to the issue (including automated emails).
- **Service Level Agreement (SLA):** Could be a doctype defining for a given priority or contract, the response and resolution targets.
- **Maintenance Schedule:** Fields - Asset or Item to maintain, schedule frequency (e.g., monthly, or specific dates), next due date. It can auto-create **Maintenance Visit** records when due.
- **Maintenance Visit/Log:** Fields - what was done, any parts used, technician, status (completed or needs follow-up).
- **Warranty Claim:** If separate, fields - Item, serial/batch (if any), issue description, verdict (approved/denied), action (repaired, replaced), and link to any supplier RMA if outwards.
- **Knowledge Base (Solution or Help Article):** Fields - title, issue symptoms, solution steps. Possibly link to related Issue or Item. Could be exposed on website or internal.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Support dashboard would show open tickets, possibly in order of priority or due date. It might have counters: "Open: 5, Overdue: 1, Awaiting Customer: 2, Total closed this month: 20" etc. A support agent (or the owner wearing that hat) can filter by status or assignee.

Logging a new issue is straightforward: perhaps a big "+ New Ticket" button, which on mobile just asks "Customer Name/Phone, Issue details" and optionally pick a type like "Product Issue / General Query". If the customer exists in CRM, selecting them could auto-fill contact details and show their purchase history (to pick which product has an issue, perhaps).

On each issue, conversation history is shown, like a thread or chat. The support person can add a note like "We will send a technician tomorrow" and mark status accordingly. If email integration is set, they could press "Reply to customer" and it would send an email (but maybe out of MVP scope; they might just call or SMS in reality, then note in system "Called customer, advised on solution").

For maintenance schedules, perhaps an interface like a calendar or list of upcoming services. The system might generate tasks or tickets for each upcoming maintenance, which appear like normal issues but internally flagged as maintenance type.

For warranty, when creating a ticket, if user selects an item that is under warranty (maybe by serial number lookup), the system could flag "Item under warranty until \[date\]" to guide how to handle (maybe free replacement).

**Offline Capabilities:** Field technicians or support staff might use the app offline when visiting a customer site. They should be able to pull up the ticket details offline (assuming it was synced beforehand) and update it (like adding resolution notes or changing status to Completed) while out of coverage, then sync later. If creating a new ticket offline (say someone complains at a remote location), it's stored and will be uploaded.

The knowledge base would likely not be accessible offline unless cached, but we might cache some frequent solutions for offline reference.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Joseph sells and services solar lamps. A customer, Mary, comes back with a lamp that isn't charging. Joseph opens the Support module on TOSS and logs a_ _Ticket_\*: "Lamp not charging", selects Mary's name from customers (or enters her contacts), and chooses category "Product Warranty". TOSS knows that lamp was sold 3 months ago with 1-year warranty (because the sales invoice and item info are linked), so it flags it as "Under Warranty". Joseph assigns the ticket to his technician, Alan.

Alan gets the ticket on his app, sees Mary's address and the issue. He goes to check the lamp. Offline at Mary's place, he opens the app to view the issue details (which were synced earlier). He finds the solar panel connection loose, fixes it on the spot. On the ticket, he adds a **Comment** "Reattached panel wires, lamp charging now" and sets status to Resolved. Mary is happy.

When Alan is back online, the ticket updates to server. Joseph sees it on his dashboard as Resolved. He calls Mary to confirm everything is fine, then closes the ticket. The system tracks that from open to close it took 2 days.

Another scenario: separately, Joseph has a fridge in his shop that needs yearly service. He entered a **Maintenance Schedule** for "Shop Fridge" to service every 12 months. TOSS reminds him a month before due via a generated maintenance ticket: "Service Shop Fridge due." He uses that prompt to schedule a technician visit for preventative maintenance. Once done, he closes that with notes "Cleaned coils, checked coolant".

For common issues, Joseph also starts building a **Knowledge Base**. For example, he got many questions about how to change the lamp battery. He writes a quick help article "How to replace solar lamp battery" in TOSS Solutions. Next time someone calls, he can refer to it, or even send them a link if the knowledge base is available on his website.

Because Joseph cares about service, he set an **SLA**: respond to all support tickets within 4 working hours. One day he misses a notification and 5 hours pass with no reply to a new ticket. TOSS flags it as breached SLA (maybe turning it red and bumping priority). Joseph then quickly calls the customer to apologize and assist, learning to keep a closer eye on those alerts.\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The AI in Support can help triage and even suggest solutions. For instance, if Mary's "lamp not charging" issue is logged, the AI could search the knowledge base and pop a suggestion: "Solution found: Check solar panel wire (common issue)" - essentially an AI-driven FAQ helper[\[61\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,tickets%20by%20connecting%20your%20email). This reduces time to resolution by guiding support staff to known fixes. If integrated with some NLP, it might categorize tickets by analyzing the description (e.g., categorize as "charging issue" vs "bulb issue").

It might also prioritize tickets based on sentiment or impact. For example, it could detect if certain keywords indicate an urgent or potentially viral complaint (like "battery exploded") and mark it high priority automatically.

AI can also analyze support trends: "In the past month, 5 tickets about lamp model X not charging - maybe a batch problem or design flaw."[\[51\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L360-L364) This insight can prompt Joseph to check that product line or inform the supplier.

For customer happiness, AI might track average resolution time and compare to satisfaction feedback. It could suggest improvements if certain issue types take too long (e.g., "Delivery delay complaints average 4 days to resolve; consider a faster process").

If multiple support agents, AI can load-balance by suggesting who should take a new ticket (based on workload or expertise).

**Collaborative Network Features:** Support collaboration across businesses might occur if multiple companies share a customer support center or escalate issues to each other. Example: A small IT support co-op where each member handles first-level support for their own clients but can escalate complex issues to a central expert group. TOSS could allow transferring a ticket to another tenant in the network (with the customer's okay presumably). The receiving party then handles it and maybe charges for it (the system could tie into inter-company billing if needed).

Another angle: if one business's product is supported by another (like a retailer logs warranty claims to the manufacturer), TOSS can facilitate creating a linked issue in the manufacturer's system. Essentially, the retailer's ticket marked as "Escalated to Supplier" can spawn an issue in the supplier's TOSS instance via network. The supplier resolves it (maybe by sending replacement), updates their issue, which then syncs back a status update to the retailer's ticket. This supply chain support integration is powerful for quick turnaround[\[48\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L430-L438).

Also, knowledge base could be shared network-wide. E.g., common troubleshooting for a device might be maintained by the manufacturer and available to all resellers' support modules. TOSS can allow certain knowledge base articles to be syndicated across tenants (so everyone gives correct info). Possibly a network support forum integration too.

Group SLAs might be established for network-driven services (like a driver co-op might promise any delivery issue is addressed within X hours by whomever is responsible). TOSS then monitors those and can show a network SLA compliance report.

In summary, the Support module primarily ensures each business handles its customer issues well, but via the network it can escalate problems to those accountable upstream (suppliers) or share expertise sideways (other similar businesses). This collective approach means a small shop is not alone in solving product issues - it has the backing of a network's knowledge and the manufacturer's direct input through the integrated system. This leads to faster resolutions and better customer service overall[\[60\]](https://zikpro.frappe.cloud/ERPNext-Helpdesk#:~:text=,that%20have%20already%20been%20set).

## POS (Point of Sale Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The POS module provides a streamlined interface for **selling products in a retail setting**, particularly optimized for counter sales and **offline functionality**[\[62\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L190-L198)[\[63\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L208-L216). It's essentially the front-end for daily sales at a shop, enabling quick billing, multiple payment modes, and receipt printing. The key goal is to make selling fast and possible without internet, syncing transactions later to the main system. This module is critical for high-volume or quick transactions, like in grocery stores, clothing shops, food stalls, etc., common in townships.

**Core Workflows:**

- **Sale Transaction Entry:** The cashier uses the POS screen to build a **cart** of items a customer is buying. They scan item barcodes or search by name, adjust quantities, and the system calculates totals with taxes/discounts if any. It's akin to creating an invoice but in a more interactive manner.
- **Multiple Payment Methods:** The customer can pay via cash, card, mobile money, or split among these. The POS module allows recording one or more payment modes per order (e.g., R50 cash, R30 card)[\[64\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L194-L202). It should also handle situations like giving change for cash.
- **Receipt Printing:** After payment, a sales receipt can be printed or sent via SMS/WhatsApp to the customer (if technology permits). The receipt shows item details, prices, total, payments, and shop info.
- **Sales Syncing:** Each sale will create a Sales Invoice or similar record in the backend. If offline, these are queued. Once online, the transactions sync to the server, updating central accounts and stock[\[65\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L200-L205).
- **Closing Day/Shift:** At day end or shift end, the cashier can do a **Cash-Up** process: the system shows how much cash should be in drawer based on sales, the cashier counts actual cash, enters it, and the system records any variance[\[19\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L234-L241). This ensures accountability and feeds into accounting.
- **Returns/Refunds:** The POS should handle simple returns or exchanges. Either by referencing the original receipt (if stored) or just doing a negative line sale. For instance, a customer returns an item bought earlier; the cashier can mark it and either give refund or allow exchange with something else.
- **Hold/Resume (optional):** In case a customer isn't done and steps aside, the cashier can hold the bill and start a new one for the next in line, then recall the held one later.
- **User Authentication:** Each cashier likely logs in with a PIN or credentials to use POS. This logs who did the sale (important for shift tracking).
- **POS Settings:** Some config like default warehouse (stock source), whether to allow sale when out-of-stock, etc., would be set per POS profile.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Stock Deduction:** The POS will reserve/deduct stock as soon as sale is completed (or when syncing). If an item is out-of-stock (and system knows it, when online), the system might warn or prevent adding it. If offline, it may allow sale but later sync might show negative stock, then management must adjust. Config might allow or block negative stock sales.
- **Pricing Accuracy:** The POS uses the price list (likely standard selling rate) and applies any tax included. It must ensure correct calculation even offline (so price list and tax rules must be cached). If a cashier tries to change a price manually (if allowed), system should log it or require a manager override if beyond allowed discount.
- **Payment Completion:** Should not finalize a sale until the payment collected equals or exceeds total (unless it's a credit sale by design, but in POS typically you settle immediately). Overpayments could be handled by issuing change. If card payment fails, allow reattempt or alternate method.
- **Receipt Sequence:** Each sale gets a unique POS invoice number (maybe separate series from regular invoices). If offline, it might number them locally, then on sync might adjust or map to a central sequence or keep the offline as a distinct series labeled by device.
- **Security:** Cashier should not be able to access more than needed (e.g., not deep accounting data). Also, once a sale is made, editing it should be restricted (returns via new transactions, not altering old ones).
- **End-of-Day Variance:** If a large variance is noted repeatedly, system may alert management (could tie into AI or at least logs these events).
- **Offline Limits:** Possibly set a limit on how many offline invoices can be made or how long to go without sync, to avoid huge backlog or misuse. But in practice, if days offline, it should accumulate and sync when possible.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **POS Profile/Settings:** Fields - link to specific Store or user, default Warehouse, default Cash account, allowed payment modes, etc. If multiple devices or branches, each might have one.
- **POS Invoice (Sales Invoice variant):** Fields - Invoice ID, date/time, items (item code, qty, price, amount), taxes, total, list of payments (mode, amount), cashier, and perhaps a link to a customer if captured (often sales are to "Walk-in" generic customer unless specifically recording).
- **POS Payment Entry (maybe embedded):** Each invoice has payments, or the invoice itself holds the multi-payment details.
- **Sales Invoice (regular):** Possibly the POS uses the same doctype as normal Sales Invoice but flagged as POS, or it has a separate queue that later creates Sales Invoices on sync.
- **Closing Voucher/Cashup record:** Could be a doctype that logs closing counts: fields - cashier, period (shift), expected cash, actual cash, variance, and remarks. This might trigger an accounting entry if needed to record any over/short.
- **POS Log/Sync Log:** internal tracking of what's synced, last sync timestamp, etc.

**User Interface & Experience:** The POS UI is distinct from the rest of the back-office. It's typically a full-screen interface with large buttons and minimal text input:

- **Item selection:** If device has a barcode scanner (or camera scan), scanning item instantly adds it to cart. Otherwise, a big search bar or category buttons allow adding items.
- **Cart view:** The right (or left) side shows the list of items chosen, with quantity and price, live-updating total. Each line can be tapped to edit quantity or remove.
- **On-Screen Keypad:** For touchscreen devices, an on-screen numeric keypad to enter custom quantities or prices.
- **Payment:** When cart is final, clicking "Pay" opens a payment modal: shows total, options for cash, card, etc., likely with quick buttons for common amounts to quickly calculate change (e.g., if total is R78 and customer gives R100, cashier enters 100 cash, system shows change R22).
- **Offline indicator:** Perhaps a small status icon showing if the device is offline (so cashier knows to inform customer maybe receipts might not be emailed or something).
- **Customer info:** Optionally capture customer phone or name for receipt (not mandatory for quick sales, but helpful for warranty or loyalty if integrated).
