- **Print/Done:** After payment, a "Print Receipt" (if printer connected) or "Send Receipt" action. Then POS resets to new sale.

The UI needs to be **fast** - minimal loading delays - because customers are waiting. Data like item list and prices are preloaded/cached to avoid any fetch delay mid-sale. If an item has variations (size, color) maybe a quick selection popup appears.

Mobile-first: Many might run POS on a tablet or even smartphone. The design should be responsive - maybe simpler on a small screen (vertical scrolling list of items to tap-add, etc.). If a dedicated device, maybe small Android tablets with barcode scanners or those all-in-one POS devices.

**Offline Capabilities:** The POS is specifically built for offline. It stores a local copy of all items, prices, taxes, and even last known stock (if needed but not critical for selling). When offline, it continues to generate sales and numbers them locally. It will queue these sales in a local database. When connectivity is restored, it automatically pushes those to the server (ensuring unique ID mapping, maybe using a device prefix or a temporary series then server consolidates them).

During offline, some features might be limited: e.g., if paying by card, that might need internet (unless it's a separate card terminal outside TOSS's scope). But cash transactions are fine offline. If it's integrated with any online loyalty or validation (like gift cards), those might not work offline unless pre-validated data is cached.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** \*Sibongile operates a busy spaza shop. She uses TOSS POS on an affordable Android tablet with a built-in scanner. Each morning, she opens the POS app and it syncs to ensure prices and stock are up-to-date. Mid-morning, the internet goes down, but she continues selling seamlessly.

A customer comes with 5 items: bread, milk, 2 soda cans, and chips. Sibongile scans each item's barcode; each beep adds the item to the list with price. The POS instantly shows the running total and any tax included (VAT is included in prices in her case). The customer has an old phone number she gave previously, Sibongile finds her in system as a regular; she decides to tag the sale to that customer to track their purchase history (maybe for loyalty points in future). The total is R96. Customer pays R100 cash. Sibongile hits "Cash", enters 100. The POS shows "Change: R4.00". She finalizes the sale, the app prints a small receipt on her Bluetooth printer. All this while offline - the customer experience is uninterrupted.

By afternoon, connectivity returns; the POS syncs all morning sales (maybe 50 transactions) to the server in the background. Inventory is reduced for each item sold, and accounting entries for daily sales aggregate into the books[\[66\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L222-L225).

Later in the day, a customer returns a pack of spoiled bread from the morning sale. Sibongile finds the receipt or the record in POS (or just trusts the customer since it's a small amount) - she uses the POS "Return Item" function: scans the bread, it shows -R12 (negative line) and processes a refund of R12 in cash. This updates inventory (one bread added back, or marked wasted if she chooses not to resell it) and logs the return.

At 7 PM, she closes the shop. The POS has a **Close Shift** routine: it shows total cash sales R800, card sales R500 for the day. Sibongile counts the cash in drawer - it's R790, R10 short. She enters actual cash R790. The system records a R10 shortfall variance[\[67\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L232-L239). She notes maybe she gave a bit extra change by mistake. This closing entry, once synced, will adjust the accounting (record that R10 as a cash short expense).

Throughout, the interface was easy: large text, simple steps. She could operate it while chatting with customers, improving speed and reducing errors. If something wasn't in the system (say a new product not entered yet), she could use a generic PLU or quickly add it at checkout with a price - the system would mark it as an open item sale (to be properly added to inventory later by management).

Thanks to POS, Sibongile can also see later which items sold most (through reports), and that data feeds into Stock module reorders, and her AI co-pilot might suggest "You sold 50 sodas today (fast mover), ensure to restock soon!"\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** AI in POS can provide smart prompts: for example, **upselling** suggestions[\[68\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L238-L241). If common combos exist (like customers who buy bread often also buy butter), the POS could alert "Suggest butter?" when bread is in cart and butter stock is available. This could increase sales per transaction.

AI also monitors **patterns**: e.g., detects if a certain time of day has peak load - it might recommend "Peak at 6-7pm, ensure two cashiers if possible." Or if certain products often cause checkout delays (maybe due to needing age verification or price lookup), it could highlight improving that.

For cash management, AI will track variances: "You have had a cash shortfall 3 days this week averaging R5. Check for error or theft patterns[\[19\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L234-L241)." If a particular cashier always has a shortage, it might discretely flag that trend.

**Sales analytics** from POS feed the AI too: daily, weekly trends, identifying top sellers, slow movers (coupling with Stock info) for the owner's dashboard, as well as detecting anomalies (e.g., "Today's sales unusually low compared to average Wednesday - was the weather bad or a competitor promotion?").

Also, AI can handle **loyalty** if implemented: e.g., "Customer X has spent R1000 here so far - consider offering a loyalty reward." Or identify new vs returning customers counts.

**Collaborative Network Features:** POS is typically local to each store, but network collaboration could come in forms of:

- **Multi-Store Data Sharing:** If one business has multiple outlets, all POS data consolidates to the central server (within same tenant). If separate businesses want to compare or share best practices, they might share aggregated metrics. Possibly a network dashboard could show average sales per store across a cooperative.
- **Unified Marketplace Integration:** If the network runs an online marketplace or group delivery system, POS could feed into it or vice versa. For example, a network might allow customers to order online from multiple shops; those orders come into each shop's POS queue for picking up or delivery packaging.
- **Cross-Store Sales:** Not common for POS, but maybe if a shop runs out of something, they could issue a sale from a neighbor's inventory (with permission). This would be more of a stock transfer sale as discussed in Stock/Collaboration.
- **Shared POS resources:** Perhaps a mobile POS that travels (like a network-hired card machine used by many small vendors on rotation). The network might have a pool of devices given to members for events - then those sales might be tagged by business and separated in the system. This is an edge case, but interesting for cooperatives at markets.

Primarily, network benefits come from combining POS data: e.g., negotiating better deals with suppliers by showing collective sales volumes. TOSS could help generate a combined sales report (if businesses agree to share that data) showing, say, total cola sales across 50 spaza shops, which they use to ask Coca-Cola for a bulk discount.

Another angle: enabling **group loyalty programs** where customers earn/redeem points across a network of shops. The POS systems across the network would need to recognize a shared loyalty account. That requires network data exchange: e.g., a central loyalty service that each POS consults (which could be TOSS's network layer hosting a multi-tenant loyalty ledger). So a customer can earn points at Shop A and spend at Shop B. Each POS call updates the central points. This fosters customer retention within the network.

In summary, the POS module directly empowers day-to-day sales especially offline. In conjunction with the network, it can elevate a local shop's capabilities to those approaching a chain, via collective analytics, shared customer programs, and supply chain leverage[\[69\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L228-L236).

## Assets (Asset Management Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Assets module is for tracking **fixed assets** owned by the business - things like equipment, machinery, vehicles, computers, furniture - basically any valuable item that has a long life and possibly depreciation. It helps keep a register of these assets, monitor their value depreciation over time for accounting, schedule maintenance, and eventually manage disposals[\[52\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=What%20features%20are%20available%20in,the%20HR%20module%20of%20ERPNext)[\[70\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=4). For township businesses, assets could include things like fridges, ovens, vehicles, solar panels, etc., which might also be provided by suppliers (like a beverage fridge from Coke). Managing these is important to ensure they are maintained and properly accounted for.

**Core Workflows:**

- **Asset Registration:** When the business acquires a new asset (purchase or donation), create an **Asset record** for it. Capture details like purchase date, cost, serial number, warranty period, supplier, etc. Assign it an ID or code. Categorize it (vehicle, appliance, IT equipment, etc.).
- **Depreciation Schedule:** Based on asset type and expected life, the system generates a **Depreciation schedule** - typically monthly or yearly depreciation entries that reduce its book value[\[52\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=What%20features%20are%20available%20in,the%20HR%20module%20of%20ERPNext). E.g., a laptop costing R12k might depreciate R200 a month over 5 years. The module can auto-post these depreciation expenses periodically.
- **Asset Value & Accounting:** The asset has an original value, current book value (after depreciation), and salvage value (expected at end). The system ensures depreciation entries hit the right accounts (debit depreciation expense, credit accumulated depreciation).
- **Maintenance & Repair Tracking:** Link with Support/Maintenance - schedule regular maintenance for assets (like service generator every 6 months), which the Support module handles (maintenance schedules & visits). Also, if an asset breaks and is repaired, log that event under the asset (with cost if any).
- **Movement/Location Tracking:** If assets can move or are assigned to people, record the **location or custodian**. E.g., "Laptop #3 assigned to employee John" or "Generator moved to Village Center site". This way, you know who is responsible for it.
- **Asset Disposal:** When an asset is sold off or scrapped, process a **Disposal**. This could create accounting entries to remove it from books (gain/loss on disposal if sold different from book value) and mark asset as retired.
- **Asset Reporting:** Provide an asset register (list of all assets with values), depreciation summary, and maybe maintenance cost per asset.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Unique Identification:** Each asset gets a unique code or tag. If physical tagging, maybe you input that code.
- **Depreciation rules:** Should follow chosen method (likely straight-line by default). The system ensures you don't depreciate past salvage or after its useful life. If purchase date mid-year, it prorates first period appropriately.
- **No Duplicate Depreciation:** If an asset's depreciation for a period is already posted, prevent posting again (or allow rollback).
- **Value Consistency:** The sum of depreciation posted plus current book value should equal original cost (less any impairment adjustments). The system should auto-calc and enforce that math.
- **Useful Life & Rate:** Need either life in years or depreciation rate (like 20% a year). Validate that input. Also salvage value must be <= cost, obviously.
- **Link to Accounting:** Each asset category might map to specific accounts (asset account, depreciation expense account). The system ensures depreciation entries use those. Possibly defined in asset category or in settings.
- **Asset State:** Only active (in-use) assets depreciate. If you pause usage (like store away), maybe still depreciate if you own it. After disposal, no further depreciation. The system stops depreciation after disposal date.
- **Maintenance Log:** Ensure any maintenance actions feed into the asset's history. If an asset is under warranty, maybe flag if trying to do a paid repair that could have been claimed.
- **Access Control:** Perhaps only managers can add/dispose assets, since it affects financials.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Asset:** Fields - Asset Name, Category (type), Purchase Date, Purchase Cost, Supplier, Serial/IMEI/etc, Assigned To (employee or department), Location, Warranty Expiry, Expected Life (or rate), Salvage Value, Depreciation Start Date, Depreciation Method, Accumulated Depreciation (computed), Current Value (computed), Status (Active, Under Maintenance, Disposed).
- **Asset Category:** Could hold default accounts and default depreciation rate/life for each category (e.g., Electronics 3 years, Furniture 5 years).
- **Depreciation Ledger/Entry:** Possibly each scheduled posting as its own doctype or the asset doctype may generate accounting entries directly. ERPNext typically creates an "Asset Depreciation Ledger" with schedule and posts Journal Entries. Fields - Asset, Date, Amount, Journal Entry link when posted.
- **Asset Value Adjustment:** If any revaluation or impairment is done (increase or write-down of value), record that. But likely out-of-scope for MVP unless needed.
- **Asset Maintenance Log:** Could just be a link to Maintenance tickets from Support. Or an internal table for each asset listing maintenance done (date, type, cost).
- **Asset Movement:** A simple child record when changing assignment/location: fields - date, from, to, person who did it.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Asset module might be used less frequently, but it should present:

- **Asset Register:** a table of all assets with key info: code, name, purchase date, cost, current value, status, location, person responsible.
- **Asset Detail Page:** shows full info and maybe quick links to related records (like open maintenance tickets for it, depreciation schedule).
- Perhaps a graph of depreciation remaining vs life (nice visual of how much value left).
- **New Asset Form:** includes financial details. Possibly integrate with Buying: e.g., when booking a Purchase Invoice for an equipment, allow "create asset from this line" which auto-fills cost and supplier.
- **Depreciation Schedule view:** On an asset page, show each period's depreciation amounts and if posted or upcoming. Possibly allow manual posting from there, or schedule automated posting (likely monthly end).
- **Maintenance**: Asset page might list last service date and next service due if schedule is set (coming from maintenance schedule in Support).
- **Disposal Wizard:** Some UI to retire an asset: input disposal date, if sold then sale amount and buyer. The system then computes gain/loss and prompts to confirm accounting entries.

Mobile usage might be limited for assets since typically it's back-office, but could allow scanning an asset tag with phone to bring up its info (for audit or maintenance on-site). E.g., tech scans fridge QR code and sees its maintenance history and enters new log.

**Offline Capabilities:** Asset data management is likely done online since it's not a high-frequency thing. But if needed, an offline scenario might be auditing assets in a warehouse with no net: user could have the list cached, tick off what they find or update location offline, then sync changes later. Not critical, but feasible.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** \*Noluthando runs a small bakery. She has a big oven, two fridges, a company motorbike for deliveries, and some industrial mixers. She records each in TOSS Assets. For her oven (cost R50k), she sets useful life 10 years, salvage R5k. TOSS schedules depreciation ~R375 per month. Each month, a Journal Entry is auto-posted to charge Depreciation Expense and reduce oven's book value by R375.

Noluthando can at any time open the Asset register to see the oven's current book value (say after 2 years, ~R41k)[\[71\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=,Provide%20valuation%20of%20each%20product). This helps for insurance or selling decisions.

Her fridges (provided by a beverage company) are technically on loan; she still lists them with a note they're supplier-owned to track maintenance but she might not depreciate them as they're not purchased assets.

The **motorbike** (cost R20k) is depreciating over 4 years. Also, she schedules maintenance: oil change every 6 months. TOSS is integrated, so a month before due, a maintenance ticket is created in Support module: "Bike ABC123: 6-month service due". She gets it serviced and logs that in the ticket (which links back to the asset record as well). She also enters that it cost R500 in that ticket; later, she can see total maintenance cost on the bike's asset page.

One day, one of her mixers breaks irreparably after 3 years. It had cost R5k with 5-year life, so book value is about R2k. She disposes it in TOSS: marks asset as sold for scrap at R1k. TOSS posts a Journal: remove asset at R5k, remove accumulated depreciation ~R3k, book R2k loss (because only got R1k for an asset with R2k book value). This keeps accounts accurate, and the asset list now shows that mixer as Disposed (so she knows not to count it in inventory of equipment)[\[72\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v12/user/manual/en/stock#:~:text=,product).

If Noluthando ever needs a loan, she has a clear record of her assets to show collateral. Also, at year-end, her accountant easily gets depreciation totals from TOSS for financial statements (no manual calc needed).\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** AI can help by monitoring asset performance and giving suggestions: - **Maintenance Prediction:** Based on usage or past issues logged, predict if an asset might fail soon. E.g., "Fridge #2 has had 3 repairs in 6 months, consider replacing it"[\[37\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L510-L514). - **Optimal Replacement Time:** Considering depreciation and maintenance costs, AI might recommend when it's more cost-effective to buy new vs maintain old. ("Your oven is fully depreciated and maintenance costs last year were high - consider a new one with energy savings features"). - **Asset Utilization:** If some assets are rarely used, AI could flag "Truck has been idle 80% of days - maybe lease it out or sell it to free capital." - **Insurance Reminder:** "Asset X's warranty or insurance is expiring next month" so she can renew or check it. - **Asset life extension**: Maybe AI suggests "Regularly cleaning oven filters could extend its life, and it's due now" tying in with support info, effectively giving proactive tips.

**Collaborative Network Features:** On a network level, assets can be part of the **sharing economy**: - **Shared Asset Registry:** The network might have a pool of shared assets (like a community generator, a delivery van, etc.). TOSS can manage those by having an asset belonging to one entity but usage schedules accessible to others. Possibly an asset could be "leased" across tenants via events. - **Group Buying for Assets:** If multiple businesses need similar equipment, network AI could identify that and suggest a group purchase to get a discount (ties with Buying collab). E.g., "5 shops need freezers; negotiate as group buy via network". - **Lending Assets:** A business could mark an asset as available for rent to others (like a heavy duty printer one shop rents evenings to neighbors). Through the network, others could request usage, and TOSS would log transfer of custody temporarily. This requires a trust layer and maybe a token exchange or so. - **Asset Transfer:** If one business closes or upgrades, they could sell an asset to another network member. TOSS can facilitate a smooth transfer: one's disposal becomes another's acquisition, possibly through a linked transaction so both records update. - **Benchmarking:** The network might gather asset reliability data. E.g., "All network bakeries using Oven Model Z had average life of 8 years with X maintenance cost - so consider that when buying new ovens." This leverages collective experience to advise individuals.

- **Insurance Negotiation:** The network could approach insurers with the collective asset base to get cheaper insurance for all. TOSS could produce a combined assets valuation report (with permission) to show total assets to insure. It might also then handle if an insurance claim is needed network can expedite it (like standardized logs from TOSS proving maintenance was done etc., easing claims).

In essence, the Assets module focuses on each business's capital goods, but network features allow them to leverage each other for better asset utilization, purchasing power, and learning from shared maintenance data[\[73\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L511-L514).

## Quality (Quality Management Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Quality module implements a **Quality Management System (QMS)** to ensure products or services meet certain standards. It covers **quality inspections, testing, non-conformance handling, and continuous improvement** activities[\[43\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,insights%20into%20production%20performance%2C%20costs). In manufacturing contexts, it's used to inspect raw materials, work-in-progress, and finished goods. In retail or service contexts, it might handle things like checking perishable stock for expiration, ensuring service procedures are followed, or customer feedback logging for quality improvement. For township businesses, formal QMS might be new, but key principles like not selling expired goods, maintaining hygiene, and delivering consistent product quality can be managed through this module.

**Core Workflows:**

- **Quality Inspection Plans:** Define **Quality Criteria** for items or processes. For example, for a batch of bread: criteria could be weight, color, taste. Or for a service (like a haircut), maybe a checklist of steps to ensure consistency. These criteria can be part of **Quality Inspection Templates** for recurring use.
- **Incoming Quality Checks:** When receiving supplies (raw materials or goods), perform a **Quality Inspection** on a sample[\[74\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,insights%20into%20production%20performance%2C%20costs). For instance, check if eggs delivered are not cracked or if flour moisture is within spec. Record results (pass/fail or numeric measurements). If an item fails, mark the lot as rejected or to be returned to supplier.
- **In-Process Inspections:** If manufacturing, at certain stages do checks. E.g., check temperature of oven, or first output piece's dimensions. Log any adjustments needed.
- **Final Inspection & Testing:** Before product is delivered or put on shelf, do a final check against spec. E.g., for a furniture piece: verify dimensions and finish quality. If passes, allow sale; if fails, classify it as second-grade or rework if possible.
- **Non-Conformance Reporting (NCR):** If a quality issue is found (product defect, process deviation, customer complaint regarding quality), raise a **Non-Conformance** record[\[29\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L426-L434). Document what went wrong, immediate correction (e.g., removed bad items), and classify severity.
- **Corrective/Preventive Action (CAPA):** For serious or recurring issues, plan **Corrective Action** to fix root cause and **Preventive Action** to avoid recurrence[\[75\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L436-L439). The module might allow linking non-conformance to a CAPA task or project. E.g., if bread often too dense, investigate recipe or oven temp (corrective action: adjust yeast quantity and train staff).
- **Quality Meetings/Reviews:** Some QMS require periodic quality meetings to review metrics and issues[\[76\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L254-L262). The module can schedule these (maybe integrated with Projects or as events) and record decisions.
- **Quality Audit/Compliance:** If there are external standards (like health code, or a certification standard), the module can store audit checklists or compliance checks to ensure readiness. Possibly tie with Support/Audits for internal audit tasks[\[77\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L466-L474).

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Mandatory Inspections:** Configure that certain items must undergo inspection at receipt or before dispatch. The system might prevent stock from being used until inspection done (if that's desired). Or at least remind the user.
- **Sampling Rules:** If not every piece is checked, define how sampling is done (like inspect 5 units out of batch of 100). The module should allow capturing how many tested and how many failed to compute acceptance.
- **Pass/Fail Criteria:** If numeric readings are logged (like thickness in mm), the system should know acceptable range from the template and auto-mark if within tolerance or not.
- **Issue Escalation:** If an inspection fails or non-conformance logged, perhaps automatically alert management if it's critical. For example, any "High severity" NCR could trigger immediate flag or create a task for CAPA with high priority.
- **Traceability:** Keep references - e.g., quality inspection should link to the batch/serial of items or the specific PO receipt. If later an issue, one can trace which batch it came from and who supplied it[\[43\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,insights%20into%20production%20performance%2C%20costs). If stock is in batches, a fail might mark that batch as quarantined.
- **Closing the Loop:** Ensure that for each non-conformance, a resolution or CAPA is eventually completed. The system might not enforce, but should encourage closing NCRs with noted actions.
- **Continuous Improvement:** Encourage using data from quality logs - e.g., trending defect rates. Possibly require monthly review of some metrics if formal.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Quality Inspection Template:** Fields - Item or Process applicable, list of Parameters (each parameter with expected range or qualitative criteria, and maybe UoM).
- **Quality Inspection:** Fields - reference (e.g., Purchase Receipt or Production Order or Batch no.), date, inspector, result for each Parameter (could be numeric value and a pass/fail or just pass/fail for that test). Overall status (Accepted/Rejected) and any remarks. Possibly attach photos (like picture of defect).
- **Non-Conformance Report:** Fields - Reference (could link to a specific job, batch, or just date), description of issue, category (supplier issue, internal process, customer complaint, safety issue, etc.), severity, immediate action taken, responsible person, and status (Open, Investigating, Resolved).
- **Corrective Action Request/Plan:** Could be a separate doctype or just fields in the NCR - describing root cause found, corrective action steps, preventive measures, who is assigned, and due date for completion. Possibly link to a Project or Task for execution.
- **Quality Meeting/Review:** If tracked, fields - date, attendees, topics discussed (like recurring high defect in X, etc.), decisions (maybe link to actions to take - which might again connect to tasks or CAPAs).
- **Quality Goals/Indicators:** Could store target metrics like "Defect rate under 2%". But likely not needed at first; can do on reports.

**User Interface & Experience:**

- For daily users (like QC inspectors or workers doing checks), a **Quality Inspection form** should be quick to fill. Possibly a mobile-friendly checklist: e.g., select batch, then a list like "Parameter: Appearance - Pass/Fail (tick or X); Parameter: Weight - input number (e.g., 500g) then system shows if pass or fail next to it." Submit yields result. On mobile, might even incorporate capturing a photo if needed (like a photo of the defect for evidence).
- For managers, a **Quality Dashboard** might show number of NCRs open, by type, and any trending issues. Possibly charts like defect rate by month, or by supplier (if lots of issues from one supplier).
- **NCR list:** A page listing open non-conformances, with filters by severity or department. Easy way to click in and update status or assign actions.
- **CAPA tracking:** perhaps integrated with Projects or a simple list of tasks generated from each NCR requiring a long-term fix. Mark them complete once done, which then can automatically close the NCR if appropriate.
- If integrated with maintenance and support: could combine audits and quality checks in one view for operations (like a store audit may double-check quality aspects, etc., but that's advanced).
- **Alerts:** if a critical issue flagged (like "contamination in product"), the system could highlight it in red, maybe even present a suggestion: e.g., "Quarantine batch, inform all customers who bought from this batch (the system could know invoices of that batch if trackable)". That would be ideal but requires lot of integration.

**Offline Capabilities:** If inspections are done on a factory floor or remote site without wifi, the user can input results offline (like via the mobile app) and sync later. Quality checks are often time-sensitive though, so likely they'd have local network at least. But offline is possible: just storing the form and sending later.

Non-conformance logging could also be offline if someone is in field noticing an issue (like a technician finds an assembly problem at a client site, logs NCR offline).

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** \*Dlamini runs a small dairy producing cheese. Quality is key since any spoilage can tarnish reputation and safety. He uses Quality module to ensure standards:

When milk is delivered daily from farmers, his assistant uses a **Quality Inspection** form: tests butterfat percentage and smell. Template says acceptable fat range 3-4%. He measures 3.5% (records it, system marks pass), smell = "normal" (qualitative pass). If any day's milk smells off or shows contamination (like a high acidity reading), he would Reject that batch - the system logs it and triggers an alert to not use that milk in production[\[43\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/manufacturing#:~:text=,insights%20into%20production%20performance%2C%20costs).

During production, they also do checks: after pasteurization, check temperature logs, etc. For each batch of cheese, before packaging, a sample is tasted and weighed. He enters those in an inspection record tied to that batch number. One time, weight was consistently 5% low on a batch - he flags that but still goes ahead, just noted for info.

Now, one week, they had 3 customer complaints of cheese getting moldy before expiry. Dlamini opens a **Non-Conformance Report** for "Cheese shelf life issue". He notes the batch numbers affected, severity medium (quality issue but not health-critical since mold is natural albeit unwanted early). He and team investigate - find that the new packaging supplier's wraps may not be sealing well.

In the NCR, he writes the suspected root cause and raises a **Corrective Action**: switch to a different packaging or improve sealing process. He sets it as a task for next week to test new packaging. Meanwhile, immediate action was to apologize to customers and replace their products (he records those replacements via support/warranty or just inventory adjustment).

He monitors that no more complaints come after they improved sealing. He then marks the NCR resolved, with a note "Switched packaging supplier, increased dryness in packaging area. No early mold observed in subsequent batches."

Also, Dlamini has periodic **Quality Meetings** with his two staff where they review any issues and ideas. TOSS might not formally record these, but he could use Projects or just notes.

Using the module, he reduces waste (by catching bad milk at intake) and improves consistency. Over months, he sees from reports that "defects per batch" is down and customer satisfaction up - valuable insights that he can also share when pursuing certifications or marketing his quality focus.\*

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** AI can significantly assist in Quality: - **Trend Detection:** It can analyze inspection data and highlight subtle trends: "The moisture content of flour has been creeping up over last 5 lots - could affect bread texture." Or "5% of items from Supplier X failed inspection in last quarter vs 1% average - maybe there's an issue[\[78\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L361-L364)." - **Predictive Quality:** Combining factors, AI might predict when processes are likely to produce defects. E.g., "Cheese mold issue likely when humidity > 80% in curing room - ensure dehumidifier use in rainy weeks" if it finds correlation between logged environmental data and defects. - **Root Cause Assistance:** For an NCR, the AI might search similar cases in the knowledge base or past records to suggest probable causes and solutions. E.g., "Early mold often due to packaging - check seal integrity" pulled from past resolved cases. - **Automated Quality Scoring:** If using visual inspection, perhaps in future hooking an AI vision to detect defects (like scanning product photos for irregularities). Possibly too advanced for now, but conceptually within AI's help in QC. - **CAPA Effectiveness:** AI can review if after certain CAPAs, relevant metrics improved or not, thus telling you if the fix truly worked or if further action needed (closing the PDCA loop). - **Regulatory Reminders:** If there are standards to maintain (like HACCP in food), AI can remind to do required checks or documentation. - Also linking with network: if a particular defect has been reported by multiple businesses in the network (all buying from same supplier), AI might connect those dots and warn everyone or escalate collectively.

**Collaborative Network Features:** Quality in a network can have a communal dimension: - **Shared Quality Standards:** If the network (like a cooperative) wants to enforce a baseline quality, they can share inspection templates or require all members to do certain checks. TOSS can push standard templates to all members' Quality module. E.g., all cooperative bakers must test bread weight, which then could be reported to central. - **Supplier Quality Management:** As in collab buying, the network can track supplier performance. If multiple members log NCRs against a supplier's product, the network leadership can aggregate that and approach the supplier for corrective action or use it as leverage for discounts/ improvements[\[29\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L426-L434). - **External Audits:** The network might collectively hire an auditor to inspect members. That auditor could have limited access to each tenant's Quality data via the network (if permitted) or TOSS could have an Audit connector. They then produce an overall compliance report, highlighting who needs improvement (like in a franchise model but here a coop model). - **Quality Benchmarking:** Compare defect rates or scrap rates across the network (anonymously or within a group). This could spur friendly competition or identify who has best practices. If one shop has nearly zero defects, others could learn from them (maybe that shop shares their process via knowledge base or training). - **Knowledge Base Sharing:** Absolutely - quality solutions and SOPs should be shareable. The network could maintain a central repository of best practices (e.g., safe food handling procedures, cleaning schedules, etc.) that all members import or reference[\[75\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L436-L439). - **Recall Management:** If a product is recalled (like a supplier issues recall on a batch of flour contaminated), through the network all businesses can be alerted and identify if they have that batch in stock (because TOSS knows batches). This quick collective response is crucial for things like food safety. The network could coordinate retrieving those products from all member shops quickly. - **Training & Certification:** The network might facilitate quality training and track who has attended. TOSS could help schedule and record such training events (slightly HR-ish but related to quality competency). - **Cooperative Quality Label:** Possibly, the network brand could have a label e.g., "Network Approved Quality" if all members adhere to certain checks. TOSS quality data could be used to prove compliance (like internal certification).

In essence, Quality module in the network fosters a culture where everyone benefits from improved quality standards - better products, fewer returns, stronger community reputation[\[79\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/toss-web/server/data/modules.ts#L480-L488). It's a key part of that third layer (collaborative network), ensuring the whole group stands for excellence.

## Website (Website & E-Commerce Module)

**Overview & Purpose:** The Website module allows businesses to create a basic web presence (and even a simple e-commerce storefront) directly from TOSS[\[80\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/website#:~:text=If%20you%27re%20not%20a%20web,Using%20this%20module%2C%20you%20can). It covers building web pages (home page, about, contact), listing products or services online, possibly blogging for marketing, and enabling an online shopping cart for customers to place orders. It essentially turns the ERP data (items, blogs, etc.) into a website without needing separate web development, which is great for small businesses who want an online footprint but can't invest in a custom site.

**Core Workflows:**

- **Website Setup:** Configure site settings - domain (maybe a subdomain on toss.net or custom domain), site name, logo, theme colors, etc.[\[80\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/website#:~:text=If%20you%27re%20not%20a%20web,Using%20this%20module%2C%20you%20can).
- **Web Pages:** Create static content pages using a CMS-like editor or templated forms. E.g., "Home", "About Us", "Contact Us". Possibly allow sections with images, text, maybe embedded map for address, etc.
- **Product Catalog:** If the business sells products, the **Item master** can be marked "Show on Website"[\[81\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/website#:~:text=,products%20using%20the%20Shopping%20Cart). Those items then appear on a product listing page (with categories). Each item will have a detail page with description, price, maybe an image gallery, and an "Add to Cart" button for e-commerce.
- **Shopping Cart & Checkout:** Customers visiting the site can browse items, add to a cart (with quantity), and then proceed to checkout. They might need to sign up or checkout as guest providing delivery info. The system generates a **Sales Order** or **Quotation** in TOSS when they place the order, which the business then processes (the workflow could integrate with Selling/CRM). Payment could be offline (like COD) or online if a payment gateway integrated (maybe not initially, but possible).
- **Contact Forms & Lead Capture:** The Contact Us page could send inquiries into TOSS as leads or support tickets. Similarly, a "Request a Quote" form could generate a lead or opportunity.
- **Blogging/News:** The module supports **Blog Posts**[\[81\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/website#:~:text=,products%20using%20the%20Shopping%20Cart). Businesses can post news, promotions, or educational content. This helps with marketing. The blog has categories and archives, etc.
- **Portal**: There might be a **Customer Portal** where customers who log in can see their orders, invoices, make payments, etc. If enabled, TOSS uses existing records to show them status (this is advanced but ERPNext does it).
- **SEO & Meta Tags:** Manage meta tags, keywords for pages to be search engine friendly. Also possibly auto-generating sitemap.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Content Approval:** Maybe not needed for a small own site, but changes might either go live immediately or require an admin user to publish.
- **Item Availability:** Only show items in stock (configurable) or at least mark if out-of-stock. Also, items may have a tick if they are available for sale online vs only in-store.
- **Pricing Consistency:** Website shows the same price as in ERP (pulls from price list). If multiple price lists (like retail vs wholesale), ensure correct one is used for site visitors (likely a default web price list).
- **Cart Stock Check:** When customer attempts checkout, check that stock is still available for those items (especially if real-time inventory display). If not, warn or prevent ordering out-of-stock items unless backorders are allowed.
- **User Accounts:** If using portal, need authentication via email/password or OTP. Basic security in place.
- **Order Confirmation:** Possibly send an email confirmation to customer on order placement. Ensure those templates are set up.
- **Payment Gateway Integration:** If implemented, handle success/cancel webhooks to mark payment status on orders.
- **Privacy/POPIA compliance:** If collecting user data, need a privacy policy page, and not misuse data. Possibly a cookie notice if needed (maybe overhead for small site, but compliance wise).
- **Multi-Tenancy for websites:** Each business likely has their own site section or subdomain. The system must isolate content per tenant obviously. If network wants a combined marketplace, that might be a separate site aggregating items from multiple tenants.

**Data Model & Key Fields:**

- **Website Settings:** Fields - site name, banner image, homepage route, etc., also toggles like "Allow signup", "Show in portal: orders, invoices, etc.".
- **Web Page:** Fields - title, route (URL path), content (could be rich text / HTML or structured blocks), published yes/no.
- **Web Menu:** For navigation bars, define menu items linking to pages or external links.
- **Blog Post:** Fields - title, content, blog category, author, published date, etc. Possibly can attach images. Blog Category (like an entity).
- **Web Slideshow / Banner:** Possibly a doctype for homepage slide show images and text.
- **Item (with Website fields):** In Item master extended fields - show on website (yes/no), website description (maybe a richer description than internal one), website image (if separate from item image), and maybe SEO meta for that item.
- **Cart/Order (for e-comm):** Possibly ephemeral until submitted. But likely just directly uses Sales Order or a separate "Shopping Cart" session object stored server-side or cookies until checkout. On submission, a Sales Order is created with link to web user.
- **Web User / Portal User:** Actually same as system user with a Customer role, limited permissions. They link to a Contact/Customer record to know whose orders to show.
- **Website Theme:** There might be a theme doctype to manage CSS, colors, etc. Or a fixed theme with minor customizations in settings.

**User Interface & Experience:**

For the business user (admin): - There might be a **Website Builder** interface to create and arrange pages. Possibly a simple WYSIWYG editor for pages content or templates to fill. It should be easy for a non-technical user to update text or add a new blog post (like writing a WordPress post). - **Preview** mode for pages before publishing changes. - A section in TOSS for Website where they manage menus, pages, and blog posts as forms. - Perhaps the .template files or pre-built design from the UI guidelines (like using Creative Tim theme) will style the site nicely by default.

For the external visitor: - The site would likely have a common header with company name/logo, nav menu, and a footer with contact details etc. - Homepage might feature a welcome message or some featured products (maybe configurable which items to feature). - If e-commerce: product listing page shows product name, thumbnail, price, maybe an "Add to cart" or link to detail. Filtering by category could be available. - Product detail page shows bigger images, description, maybe reviews (unlikely unless added later) and add to cart form (quantity and add). - The cart page shows chosen items, allows adjustments, then a checkout form for address and contact, then final confirmation. - If portal login: a login/register page. Portal dashboard with maybe "My Orders, My Invoices, My Profile". - Also pages like About Us (with rich text content describing business), Contact (with a form and contact info). - The design should be mobile-responsive, given many might browse on phones.

**Offline Capabilities:** The website is inherently an online feature. However, the PWA aspect could allow some offline browsing if cached (like last viewed pages), but that's advanced. For the admin, editing site requires connection to the server obviously. So offline not applicable here.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** \*Mama Thandi runs a crafts business (woven baskets, mats). She wants to reach more customers outside her immediate area. Using TOSS Website, she sets up an online storefront:

She goes to Website module, enters a catchy site title "Thandi's African Crafts". She uploads her logo. She writes an **About Us** page talking about her story and community impact. She creates a **Contact Us** page with her shop address, phone, and a form that visitors can submit inquiries (which TOSS will log as leads in CRM).

She has 10 product types. In the Item master, each item (like "Large Woven Basket") already had descriptions and prices for ERP. She adds a nice photo to each and marks "Show on website". She writes a bit more marketing description in the "website description" field (like emphasizing it's hand-made, dimensions, etc.). TOSS generates a product listing automatically by category (baskets vs mats), which she can reorder or refine.

Now her site is live at something like toss.site/thandicrafts (or a custom domain if she set one). A customer in another town finds it via Google (the site is simple but has her blog posts about weaving which show up in search). They browse her products, add a couple to cart, and place an order for delivery.

TOSS captures this order as a **Sales Order** under Mama Thandi's account, marked as from Website. She gets alerted in TOSS "New Online Order #1001". Since she hasn't integrated online payments yet, the site is set to "Cash on Delivery". She contacts the customer for delivery arrangements (maybe she could integrate with a driver network from the collab layer for shipping).

She fulfills the order and marks it as delivered in TOSS, and could then email an invoice. The customer upon logging in can see the status "Delivered" and maybe leave feedback.

Additionally, Mama Thandi writes periodic **Blog Posts** on her site about the significance of certain weaving patterns. Locals and even some international visitors read these, raising her profile. This content marketing helps drive traffic to her site, and she notices an uptick in online inquiries (which feed into CRM leads).

All of this, she did without hiring a web developer - just using TOSS's built-in website builder. It's not a fancy custom site, but it is good enough to showcase her products and accept orders, which is a huge leap for her business.\*[\[82\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/website#:~:text=Websites%20are%20a%20core%20component,and%20it%20not%20being%20interactive)

**SaaS 2.0 (AI & Insights):** The AI can assist with: - **SEO suggestions:** e.g., advise adding certain keywords to product pages or blog posts, or suggest "Your page title is a bit long, shorten for better search ranking". - **Content creation help:** maybe even help draft blog posts or product descriptions by providing templates or analyzing what attracts customers (maybe integrated with a language model). - **Product recommendation and personalization:** if portal users log in, AI could suggest products they might like based on past orders or browsing (like simple "customers who bought this also liked that" which could be gleaned from network data if enough volume). - **Web analytics:** Provide insight on website traffic and behavior: "Your site got 500 visits this week (up 10%). Most viewed product: Woven Mat. Consider promoting that." or "Many users drop off at checkout - maybe simplify the checkout process". - **Customer reviews sentiment:** If the site collects feedback or reviews, AI can analyze sentiment and highlight common praises or issues. - **Optimal posting times:** For her blog, AI might suggest when to post or what topics (like noticing which posts get more views or shares). - Possibly tie into social - not exactly website, but AI might recommend sharing new blog post to a linked Facebook page to drive traffic (though that is more external integration).

**Collaborative Network Features:** The network could leverage websites as: - **Central Marketplace:** Imagine a network site listing all member products (like an online mall). TOSS could aggregate items from multiple tenants into one front-end (with proper multi-tenancy handling of orders). Perhaps an advanced concept, but doable if the network chooses to have a unified e-commerce portal (customers can order from multiple shops at once; TOSS splits the order to each vendor's Sales Orders and coordinates payments and deliveries across them). This is complex but a powerful network synergy - small businesses get an exposure as if one big platform (like Etsy style but local). - **Shared Content:** The network could maintain a blog for the community or share content. For instance, a business might allow the network to automatically display relevant posts or adverts. Or a cooperative could push announcements to member sites (like "Shop Local Week promotion" banner shows on all member's websites). - **Domain & Hosting support:** The network might handle custom domain setup or ensure hosting. If a member can't afford domain, they can have a subdomain on the network's domain. If network invests in better server/backbone, all benefit (TOSS cloud presumably covers hosting though). - **Training customers to use portal:** If multiple businesses in network adopt TOSS website, they can collectively educate the community on using these online shops, possibly unify login (like one network login can access all portal if some SSO implemented - maybe far-fetched, but conceptually a "One login for township marketplace" could be nice). - **Data sharing for better SEO:** Network could ensure cross-linking between member sites to improve search rankings (like a directory of local businesses with links to each site). - **Security and updates:** The network ensures that all member websites get timely security updates or upgrades (TOSS does that centrally anyway). Possibly also content moderation if needed (to ensure nothing inappropriate, if network brand is attached). - **Collective analytics:** The network can see aggregate web analytics to understand overall demand trends. If many searches or hits for "handmade baskets", network could encourage more members to list such or do group promotions.

In short, the Website module allows each small business to punch above its weight online, and the network can amplify that by creating a local digital marketplace where all members are visible and easily accessible to customers beyond foot traffic[\[81\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/website#:~:text=,products%20using%20the%20Shopping%20Cart).

(Each module above is thoroughly detailed in the context of TOSS, drawing parallels to ERPNext modules and tailoring them to the township business scenario. The SaaS 2.0 and network aspects are integrated or appended to each section, as requested, and there's alignment with references and guidelines from ERPNext documentation and TOSS vision documents throughout.)

# TOSS Platform Functional Specification v1.0

## Introduction

**TOSS (The One-Stop Solution)** is a next-generation ERP-III platform tailored for South African township and rural businesses. It combines a full suite of ERP modules with intelligent _Service-as-Software (SaaS 2.0)_ features and a _Collaborative Network_ layer to help small businesses not just manage operations, but also gain insights and work together as a community[\[1\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L52-L60)[\[2\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L118-L126). The system is **offline-first and mobile-first**, delivered as a Nuxt 4 Progressive Web App for low-end Android devices, and powered by a multi-tenant, event-driven .NET 8 backend (Clean Architecture with PostgreSQL)[\[3\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L263-L271)[\[4\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L243-L250). Every design choice aligns with ERPNext's proven ERP module concepts[\[9\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L160-L169), adapted to be simpler and more context-appropriate for users like spaza shop owners, hawkers, small-scale manufacturers, and other township entrepreneurs.

**Product Pillars:** The platform consists of three integrated layers[\[6\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L90-L98):

- **ERP-III Modules (Business Backbone):** Traditional ERP domains (Sales, Purchasing, Accounting, Stock, etc.) providing the essential tools to run a business.
- **SaaS 2.0 (AI Business Coach):** An AI-driven layer that watches business data and proactively suggests actions or automations (acting as a "business manager with an MBA")[\[7\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L110-L118).
- **Collaborative Network:** Multi-tenant capabilities that let independent businesses cooperate - pooling orders, sharing resources, and collectively negotiating as a network[\[8\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L120-L124).

In the sections below, each ERP module is specified in detail - including its purpose, key workflows, business rules, data model, UI/UX expectations (with offline functionality), and an example use case in a township/rural context. Subsequent sections describe how the AI SaaS layer and Collaborative Network layer augment these modules with insights and cross-organization workflows. All functionality is aligned with ERPNext's documented features for familiarity and robustness[\[5\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L158-L166), while ensuring the solution remains **simple, offline-capable, and intuitive** for the target users[\[11\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L54-L61).

## Selling (Sales & Marketing Module)

**Functional Overview & Purpose:** The Selling module in TOSS streamlines the entire sales process from initial customer inquiry to final sale, while also helping manage customer relationships. It covers customer inquiries, quotations, sales orders, deliveries, and invoicing - integrating closely with CRM and Accounting. In essence, this module helps businesses efficiently **generate and track sales** and maintain customer info to improve service and drive revenue growth[\[12\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=The%20Selling%20module%20in%20ERPNext,and%20enhance%20customer%20relationship%20management)[\[15\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,trends%20to%20inform%20strategic%20decisions). It also supports basic marketing functions like tracking campaigns or customer referrals relevant to township businesses (e.g. loyalty programs or word-of-mouth promotions).

**Core Workflows:** Key workflows in Selling include:

- **Lead-to-Quote:** Capture a lead or inquiry (via CRM) then create a **Quotation** (sales quote) for the products/services the customer is interested in. Quotations can be sent to customers and later converted to orders[\[14\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,on%20sales%20performance%2C%20revenue%2C%20and).
- **Order Fulfillment:** Convert an accepted quotation into a **Sales Order**. The Sales Order is the confirmed customer order, which initiates reservation of stock. From the Sales Order, generate a **Delivery Note** (for physical goods) to ship items, and finally create a **Sales Invoice** to bill the customer[\[14\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,on%20sales%20performance%2C%20revenue%2C%20and).
- **Direct Sale (POS):** For walk-in or counter sales, use the POS sub-module for a quick invoice and immediate payment (see **POS module** below). POS sales automatically deduct stock and create accounting entries on sync.
- **Returns & Credit Notes:** If a customer returns a product, record a **Sales Return** (Credit Note) which updates stock and creates a credit/refund record in accounting.
- **Customer Management & Follow-up:** Maintain a master list of **Customers** with contact info, delivery addresses, and perhaps loyalty details. Track communication leading up to a sale (linked emails/calls via CRM) so that all quotes and orders are in context[\[15\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/selling#:~:text=,trends%20to%20inform%20strategic%20decisions). Payment terms and credit limits per customer can be enforced to manage credit sales (e.g., block new orders if a customer exceeds their credit limit).

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Quotation Validity & Approval:** Quotations carry an expiry date; the system prevents converting an expired quote to an order without extension. Optionally, set approval requirements for quotes giving large discounts or special terms.
- **Stock Reservation:** Confirming a Sales Order will allocate stock from inventory (if the item is stock-managed). The system will not allow delivery of more than the ordered quantity or more than what's available in stock (unless backordering is allowed). If an item is out-of-stock at order time, the system can flag it for purchase or transfer.
- **Pricing and Discounts:** The module enforces the price list rates by default. If a salesperson applies a manual discount beyond a certain threshold, it can require manager approval. TOSS supports promotional pricing rules and coupon codes like ERPNext, but in simpler form (e.g., an automatic 10% off on certain items during a sale period)[\[16\]](https://9t9it.com/eprnext-faq#:~:text=What%20features%20are%20available%20in,the%20Sales%20module).
- **Status Transitions:** Documents follow defined statuses - e.g., Quotation (Draft → Submitted → Ordered/Lost), Sales Order (Draft/Confirmed → Partly Delivered → Completed/Closed). The system automatically updates status based on actions (e.g., marking a Sales Order as Completed once fully delivered and invoiced).
- **Customer Credit Control:** If a customer has exceeded their credit limit or has overdue invoices, TOSS can warn or block new Sales Orders for that customer (configurable). This prevents overextending credit to customers who might default.
- **Integration with Accounting:** Posting a Sales Invoice will automatically update the Accounts Receivable for that customer and record revenue. The module ensures each invoice has proper tax calculations and accounting impact. In TOSS, however, accounting jargon is minimized - for example, users see "Money In" entries rather than "debit to debtor account" (the underlying double-entry happens invisibly).

**Required Data Models & Key Fields:** Important DocTypes in Selling include:

- **Customer:** Stores customer details (Name, contact info, customer type/territory, credit limit, default price list, etc.).
- **Quotation:** Key fields - Customer, Valid Till Date, Item table (items, quantities, rates, any discount), Taxes/charges, Total amount, Status. It may also include terms or notes for the quotation.
- **Sales Order:** Key fields - Customer, Delivery Date, Item table (with quantities and rates locked in), workflow Status, and links to subsequent Delivery Notes and Invoices. Has flags like _"Drop-ship"_ or _"Maintenance Required"_ if relevant.
- **Delivery Note:** Fields - Linked Sales Order (optional), Items delivered (with actual quantities, batch/serial numbers if tracking), Delivery Date, and status (Draft, Submitted, etc.). This updates stock levels.
- **Sales Invoice:** Fields - Customer, Invoice Date, Due Date, Item table (quantities, rates), Taxes, Totals, Payments (if paid immediately), and status (Unpaid/Paid/Cancelled). In TOSS, a Sales Invoice can be used for immediate payment scenarios (POS) or credit sales (with later payment entry).
- **Payment Entry (for Sales):** If customers pay after invoicing, a Payment Entry record links the payment to one or multiple invoices, recording the date, mode (cash, bank, mobile money), and amount received[\[39\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/v13/user/manual/en/accounts#:~:text=In%20ERPNext%2C%20accounting%20operations%20consists,of%203%20main%20transactions).
- **Pricing Rule:** (If used) Defines special pricing or discounts for certain conditions (e.g., customer group, quantity break). Key fields - applicable item/customer, min quantity, rate or discount percentage.

**User Interface & Experience:** The Selling module's UI is designed to be friendly and accessible on mobile devices. Transaction forms use **plain, friendly language** instead of accounting jargon[\[18\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L294-L301). For example, the Sales Invoice form might label fields as "Money Received?" instead of "Is Paid," and show "People who owe you" for the receivables list[\[18\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L294-L301).

Creating a new sale is straightforward: a user can tap **"New Sale Order"** and then select a customer (with an option to quickly add a new customer if not already in the list). They then add items by typing the first letters or scanning a barcode (the app provides typeahead search through the item list). On a phone, items can be added via a plus-button or by entering a SKU. The form automatically computes totals and applicable taxes. The UI supports splitting an order into multiple deliveries (for backorders) with a clear "Delivered" vs "Pending" status on each item line.

Mobile-first design means forms are broken into sections that can collapse for ease of navigation. For instance, on a small screen, the Sales Order form might first show "Customer & Date" section, then an "Items" section, then a "Summary & Submit" section. This avoids one long scrolling form. There's also a prominent **Submit/Confirm** button at the end to finalize the order.

Throughout the UI, the terminology is simplified: "New Sale" (Sales Order), "Send Bill" (Invoice), "Record Payment" instead of "Journal Entry"[\[18\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L294-L301). The module also uses a **topbar search** where a user can search for any sales document by customer name or item, and TOSS will bring relevant results (leveraging global search).

**Offline Capabilities:** Core sales flows are supported offline for resiliency. Sales Orders and Invoices can be **created offline** if the device is not connected - they will be stored locally in the app's database. Each offline transaction gets a temporary ID. Once connectivity is restored, the app syncs these to the server, which assigns official numbers and integrates them into stock and accounts. In practice, for a typical sales order (which usually might be taken when somewhat online), offline is less common than in POS, but it's possible (e.g., writing an order at a remote client site). The system's design ensures that even if multiple offline orders are queued, when syncing it resolves any numbering or stock allocation conflicts gracefully (using timestamps and device IDs)[\[35\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L316-L324).

For example, a salesperson out in the field can create a quote or order on their phone without network. The customer's details and item catalog are cached, so selection is easy. Later, when back online, the quote syncs to the server and can be emailed out. The app will alert the user of any sync issues (say, if an item was discontinued during that period, it will flag it for correction). Overall, offline mode in Selling ensures no sale is lost just because of connectivity, and it queues all updates (stock, ledger entries) to apply once online.

**Example Use Case (Township Context):** _Naledi runs a small hardware store in a township. Using the Selling module, she handles both walk-in customers and bulk orders from local contractors. A contractor comes in requesting a quote for 100 bags of cement and 20 steel pipes. Naledi quickly creates a_ _Quotation_ _on her tablet, selecting the customer (who is already in her CRM) and the items; the system pulls in her standard prices. She adds a note "Valid for 7 days" and sends it via WhatsApp directly from TOSS (the quotation PDF is generated in-app). The contractor confirms the next day, so Naledi converts that quote to a_ _Sales Order_\* with one tap. The stock for 100 cement and 20 pipes is now reserved under that order.

Naledi sees in TOSS that she only has 80 bags of cement in stock (20 short). The system, via the Stock module integration, automatically flags a **material shortage** for cement. She quickly creates a Purchase Order to her supplier for the remaining 20 (from the Buying module). Meanwhile, she partially fulfills the sales order: she delivers the 80 bags available, generating a **Delivery Note** and updating the order status to "Partly Delivered". The customer is fine with a split delivery.

Once the remaining cement arrives the next day, Naledi delivers them and the Sales Order is completed. TOSS generates a **Sales Invoice** for the full 100 bags and 20 pipes, since the order is now fully delivered. The contractor has 30-day payment terms. TOSS tracks this in Accounts Receivable (Naledi can see the invoice under "People who owe you" with due date)[\[18\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L294-L301).

At month-end, Naledi reviews her sales in the dashboard: she sees total sales, and specifically that contractor's large order is listed, helping her manage cash flow expectations. Because she recorded everything through the Selling module, her stock levels and financials stayed accurate throughout, and she maintained a professional interaction (quotes, invoices) with minimal effort.\*

**SaaS 2.0 - AI & Insights:** The Selling module is enhanced by AI-driven insights that act like a smart sales assistant. For example, the system can analyze customer buying patterns and suggest **upsell or cross-sell opportunities** to increase sales. When creating a sales order, TOSS might prompt: "Customers who bought cement often buy sand - add sand to this order?" based on historical data. The AI also keeps an eye on pricing and margins - if a salesperson gives an unusually large discount that brings margin below a set threshold, the system can flag it: _"Warning: Very low margin on Item X"_[\[83\]](https://github.com/Toss-Online-Services/TossErp/blob/10c8061dab87e2b12429c455fe4113e62a69f8e0/.cursor/rules/toss.mdc#L112-L117). It could require manager approval or at least log this event for review, preventing inadvertent loss-making deals.

TOSS's AI "business coach" monitors sales trends and customer behavior. It might highlight that a formerly regular customer hasn't ordered in a while and suggest reaching out (a nudge to use the CRM for a follow-up call). It can also identify top customers and prompt Naledi with a message like: _"Thabo's Workshop has purchased R5,000 of goods this month - consider offering a loyalty discount or a thank-you note."_ These relationship-building cues help retention.

On a broader level, AI analyzes sales performance against targets. If it knows Naledi's weekly sales goal (she can set one), it can notify mid-week: _"You are 70% to your sales goal by Wednesday - on track!"_ or _"Sales are slower than usual this week, consider a promotion or SMS campaign to boost footfall."_ These friendly prompts in plain language help a busy shopkeeper take quick action.

**Collaborative Network Features:** Within a network of businesses, the Selling module enables cooperative sales and shared opportunities. For example, businesses can engage in **group sales or bulk deals** that they advertise collectively. If multiple shops form a buying group to negotiate better prices (see Buying module), they could also collectively offer a promotion (e.g., a township-wide sale event) to increase volume. The network layer might facilitate a **shared marketplace**: each shop's products could be listed on a central marketplace site (see Website module), effectively pooling their catalogs to attract more customers together than individually. Orders from that marketplace would route to the respective shop's Selling module for fulfillment.

In addition, the collaborative network allows referral sales: one business can refer a customer to another if they don't stock a requested item. Through TOSS, if Shop A doesn't have cement but knows Shop B in the network does, Shop A could create a referral sales order that Shop B fulfills. The system could credit Shop A with a referral commission automatically. This encourages businesses to **cross-refer** rather than let a customer leave the network.

The network layer can also share **sales insights across the community** (without revealing individual company data unless allowed). For instance, it could show to members: "Collectively, spaza shops in Network X sold 5000 loaves of bread this week." This kind of aggregate data might help each shop gauge demand trends or negotiate with bakeries as a group. If one shop's sales of a certain product are skyrocketing (maybe due to a local event or promotion), the network can propagate that knowledge so others can stock up and benefit too.

Lastly, collaborative selling efforts such as **group loyalty programs** can be managed. Customers could earn loyalty points across the entire network of shops (e.g., a customer earns points buying from Shop A and can redeem at Shop B). The Selling module, via the network, would update a central loyalty ledger. This drives customer stickiness to network businesses rather than to outside competitors. Overall, collaboration in selling transforms what individual small shops can do by themselves into what a coordinated group can achieve - whether it's bulk promotions, shared customers, or simply learning from each other's sales patterns.

## Buying (Procurement Module)

**Functional Overview & Purpose:** The Buying module manages the procurement process end-to-end, helping businesses efficiently purchase goods and services and maintain healthy supplier relationships. It covers everything from requesting supplier quotes, placing purchase orders, receiving goods into stock, to handling supplier invoices. Essentially, this module ensures that **stock is replenished** in a timely and controlled manner and that **purchases are cost-effective**[\[20\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=The%20Buying%20module%20in%20ERPNext,processes%20and%20optimise%20supplier%20relationships)[\[21\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment). For small businesses, this means simplifying tasks like reordering inventory and keeping track of payables so they can control costs and avoid stockouts.

**Core Workflows:**

- **Material Request (Requisition):** An internal request for items needed - e.g., a shop staff notices sugar is low and creates a **Material Request** for 50 kg of sugar. This is an optional step in TOSS (some might go straight to ordering), but useful for larger operations or for planning. Material Requests can later be merged into Purchase Orders.
- **Request for Quotation (RFQ):** If price comparison is needed, create an RFQ to send to multiple suppliers. In TOSS, you can note which items need quotes; the system can generate an email or print-out to send to chosen suppliers, requesting their prices. When they respond, you record their quotes (Supplier Quotation documents).
- **Supplier Quotation Evaluation:** Compare received quotes side-by-side (the system can tabulate price, terms, etc. for each supplier). Choose the best offer and convert it into a **Purchase Order**.
- **Purchase Order (PO):** Place the order with the chosen supplier. The PO specifies items, quantities, agreed prices, and expected delivery date[\[22\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment). Once submitted, the PO in TOSS is a formal commitment and it will reflect as "on order" stock. The system can email the PO to the supplier or generate a printout.
- **Goods Receipt:** When the supplier delivers, create a **Purchase Receipt** (Goods Received Note) to record the actual quantities received for each item. If an item is short or damaged, note it; the PO remains open for pending items or you initiate a return. Upon submission of a Purchase Receipt, inventory levels increase for those items in the specified warehouse.
- **Purchase Invoice:** Receive the supplier's bill and create a **Purchase Invoice** to record the amount owed. If the supplier invoice matches the PO/receipt, it's straightforward - TOSS copies the data from the PO or receipt. If there are differences (price changes, extra charges like shipping), you can adjust on the invoice. Submitting the Purchase Invoice will update Accounts Payable (the system records that you owe the supplier money)[\[84\]](https://docs.frappe.io/erpnext/user/manual/en/buying#:~:text=,levels%20and%20manage%20stock%20replenishment).
- **Payment to Supplier:** When you pay the supplier (advance, on delivery, or credit term), record a Payment Entry (or mark invoice as paid) to clear the liability. TOSS can handle partial payments and will show outstanding balances per supplier.

**Business Rules & Validation:**

- **Order Authorization:** Optionally require approval for POs above certain amounts (to enforce spend control). This can be configured via workflow if needed.
- **Three-way Match:** TOSS facilitates matching the PO, Receipt, and Invoice. If a Purchase Invoice is entered for more quantity than received or higher price than in PO, the system flags it. Minor variances can be allowed within a tolerance. This ensures you only pay for what was actually received and agreed. For example, if the PO was 100 units at R50 but only 90 delivered, it will warn if invoiced for 100 or if price increased unless you adjust the records intentionally.
- **Stock Update Accuracy:** A Purchase Receipt cannot be submitted without specifying the warehouse for stock and (if enabled) batch or serial numbers for items that require them. Also, if an item is found defective at receipt, it can be marked as rejected - the system keeps it out of salable stock and optionally tracks it for return to supplier.
- **Supplier Management:** Each **Supplier** has a record with terms (e.g., payment 30 days, preferred currency) and perhaps a score. The system can track statistics like on-time delivery rate by supplier. This is more data for insight but no strict rule unless set (e.g., could block new PO to a blacklisted supplier).
- **Costing Impacts:** If an item is inventory, its valuation can include additional costs like shipping or customs. TOSS allows landing cost allocation (prorating freight, etc., into item cost) though small businesses might use a simpler approach (just record such costs as expenses). By rule, if using the feature, every landed cost must be allocated fully to avoid cost discrepancies.
- **Budget Awareness:** If the business has expense budgets (not common in micro businesses), TOSS can warn when a purchase will exceed a budget (e.g., monthly purchasing budget for a category).
- **Required Fields:** Ensure key info is filled - you cannot submit a PO without a supplier, or a receipt without items and quantities, etc. If using taxes, tax template or rates should be selected to compute tax on purchase.

**Required Data Models & Key Fields:** Key DocTypes in Buying:

- **Supplier:** Master for suppliers (Name, default currency, payment terms, contact details). It can also have a credit limit or an indicator if the supplier is also a customer (some businesses buy and sell from each other).
- **Item (Purchase Info):** In the Item master, fields like default supplier, last purchase rate, and re-order level are maintained. These inform procurement decisions.
- **Material Request:** Fields - requested items (item code, quantity, required by date), request type (purchase or stock transfer), and status (Draft, Approved, Ordered, etc.). Often the first step in a workflow, can be skipped for direct POs.
